الحجة فيه؟ وما يدريكم أن الفلك لا يجوز أن يسكن يوماً ما ولا أن يتحرك حركة مستقيمة في إحدى الجهات الست وإن كنتم لم تجدوا ذلك قط؟ فإن قالوا : لأن ذلك لو جاز لجاز أن يتحرك الماء والأرض سَوْمَ أنفسهما إلى فوق، وأن تتحرك النار سَوْمَ نفسها إلى أسفل، قيل لهم : ما أنكرتم من جواز ذلك، إن كان ها هنا متحرك يتحرك سَوْمَ نفسه بغير محرك يحركه؟ وما وجودكم لتَعَذَّر هذا اليوم ما يدل على استحالته. ثم يقال لهم : ما الدليل أولاً على أن ها هنا متحركاً يتحرك سَوْمَ نفسه بغير محرك يحركه ويخترع فيه الحركة أو من غير أن يكون قادراً على تحريك نفسه ومختاراً لذلك؟ فلا يجدون إلى تصحيح ذلك سبيلاً.

ثم يقال لهم : فيجب على اعتلالكم هذا استواء طبع الهواء والنار والماء والأرض لأن النار والهواء يتحركان أبداً صُعُداً سَوْمَ أنفسهما ولا يتحركان في غير هذه الجهة فيجب استواء طبعهما لاستواء حركتيهما إن كان اختلاف الحركات دالا على اختلاف الطباع؛ وكذلك يجب اتفاق طبع الماء والأرض لاتفاق حركتيهما إلى جهة السفل وهذا ترك لقولهم إن الماء رطب والأرض يابسة والهواء رطب والنار يابسة. فإن قالوا : الأرض أقرب حركة إلى المركز من الماء فوجب اختلاف طبعيهما، قيل لهم : فوجب مخالفة طبع الصفحة التي نحن عليها من الأرض لطبع الصفحة التي تلي المركز لأن ذلك أقرب حركة إلى المركز؛ وكذلك القول في ترتيب الصفحات وهذا ترك قولهم.

ويقال لهم : ويجب على اعتلالكم هذا أن تقضوا على اتفاق طبع كلية الماء والأرض والنار والهواء لأن من طبع كليات هذه الأشياء الوقوف في عالمها الذي هو موضع مركزها وأن لا تتحرك عنه فإن صاروا إلى ذلك تركوا قولهم، وإن قالوا : اتفاق كليات هذه الأشياء في السكون في مراكزها ومواضع كلياتها لا يدل على اتفاق طبعها قيل لهم : وكذلك اختلاف حركات جزئياتها الموجودة في عالمنا لا يدل على اختلاف طباعها ولا فصل في ذلك.

ويقال لهم أيضاً: يجب على موضوعكم هذا أن يكون طبع جزئيات هذه الأشياء مخالفاً لكلياتها وأن تكون طباعها خلاف طباع كلياتها؛ وذلك أن من شأن هذه الجزئيات الموجودة في عالمنا الحركة ومن شأن كلياتها السكون والوقوف فيجب لذلك اختلاف طباع الجزئيات والكليات؛ فإن مروا على ذلك تركوا قولهم؛ وإن أبوه قيل لهم : فما أنكرتم أيضاً من اتفاق طبع الفلك والنار والهواء والماء والأرض وإن اختلفت حركات هذه الأمور؟ فلا يجدون إلى دفع ذلك سبيلاً.
What is the proof for it? And how do you know that the celestial sphere cannot come to rest one day, nor move in a straight line in one of the six directions, even if you have never observed that? If they say: because if that were possible, then water and earth could move upwards by themselves, and fire could move downwards by itself. It is said to them: Why do you deny that possibility, if there exists here something that moves by itself without a mover that moves it? And your experience of its impossibility today does not prove its impossibility. Then it is said to them: First, what is the proof that there exists something that moves by itself without a mover that moves it and invents motion in it, or without being able to move itself and choosing that? Then they can find no way to verify that.

Then it is said to them: According to this reasoning of yours, it would be necessary that the nature of air, fire, water, and earth be the same, because fire and air always move upward by themselves and do not move except in that direction; therefore their natures must be the same since their motions are the same, if differences in motion indicate differences in natures. Similarly, it would be necessary that the natures of water and earth be the same because their motions are the same downward. This negates their statement that water is moist and earth is dry, and air is moist and fire is dry. If they say: Earth is closer in motion to the center than water, so their natures must differ. It is said to them: Then the nature of the surface we are on must differ from the nature of the surface adjacent to the center, because that one is closer in motion to the center. And the same applies to the arrangement of the surfaces. This negates their statement.

And it is said to them: According to this reasoning of yours, you must judge that the universal natures of water, earth, fire, and air are the same, because it is the nature of the universals of these things to rest in their own world, which is the place of their center, and not to move from it. If they adhere to that, they negate their own statement. If they say: The agreement of the universals of these things in resting at their centers and their universal places does not indicate agreement in their natures. It is said to them: Likewise, the difference in the movements of their particulars existing in our world does not indicate a difference in their natures, and there is no distinction in that.

And it is also said to them: According to this principle of yours, the nature of the particulars of these things must be different from their universals, and their natures must be contrary to the natures of their universals. That is because the property of these particulars existing in our world is motion, and the property of their universals is rest and stillness, so the natures of the particulars and universals must differ. If they go along with that, they negate their own statement. If they refuse, it is said to them: Then why do you also deny that the natures of the celestial sphere, fire, air, water, and earth are the same, even if the motions of these things differ? Then they can find no way to repulse that.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical refutation of the doctrine that bodies have inherent natures (ṭabā’iʿ) that cause their characteristic motions. Baqillani engages with opponents who claim that the elements (fire, air, water, earth) move by their own essence without an external mover. He begins by questioning the basis for denying that the celestial sphere could ever rest or move rectilinearly, pointing out that lack of experience does not prove impossibility. He then challenges the very premise that there is something moving by itself without a mover. 

Next, he reduces their position to absurdity: if differences in motion indicate differences in nature, then since fire and air both move upward, their natures must be identical; similarly water and earth both move downward, so their natures must be identical. This contradicts the opponents' own claims about the qualities moist/dry. If they try to avoid this by citing degrees of closeness to the center, Baqillani shows that this leads to an infinite regress of differing natures among layers of earth. 

He then extends the argument to universals (kulliyyāt) versus particulars (juz’iyyāt). If universals of the elements rest at their centers while particulars move, then by the opponents' logic the natures of universals and particulars would have to differ, contradicting the idea of a single nature per element. Finally, he forces them to either accept that all elements have the same nature (since they all have a universal nature of resting) or admit that differing motions do not prove differing natures. The passage ends by asserting that the opponents have no way to refute this.

Key Terms
كلية (kulliyya) - universal
جزئية (juz’iyya) - particular
طبع (ṭabʿ) - nature
سكون (sukūn) - rest

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani argue follows from the fact that universal natures of the elements rest at their centers?
A) Their universal natures must be the same.
B) Their particular natures must be the same.
C) The celestial sphere must have a different nature.
D) The universals and particulars must have the same nature.

Key Takeaway
By forcing the opponents to consider universals versus particulars, Baqillani shows that their own principle leads to contradictions, leaving them with no consistent theory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are confronted with a contradiction in your own beliefs—like the opponents in this passage whose principle leads to absurdity—do you resort to special pleading or rationalization? Think of a specific time you dodged a logical consequence in your faith or worldview. Will you now commit to following the logic wherever it leads, even if uncomfortable?
?
Baqillani shows that the opponents had to choose between accepting a contradiction or abandoning their position. Are there areas in your life where you hold onto contradictory beliefs simply because changing would be costly or unsettling? What would it really cost you to seek consistency?
?
This passage uses universals and particulars to expose flawed assumptions. Do you ever assume that what you observe about particulars (e.g., your current state, your community) applies universally to God's nature or His actions? How might that assumption be a form of the same error Baqillani targets?

The Elements' Universals and Particulars
Baqillani refutes the claim that differing movements prove differing natures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the difference in movements of the elements' particulars does not prove a difference in their natures, and that the opponent's position leads to contradiction.

Core Idea
Movement differences do not entail nature differences.

This passage presents a key dialectical argument by Imam al-Baqillani against an opponent who claims that the natural rest of the elements' universals proves something about their nature, while the motion of particulars suggests difference. Baqillani systematically refutes this by showing that the opponent's own reasoning is inconsistent and leads to absurd conclusions. As you read, follow the conditional moves and see how he turns the opponent's premise against them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Baqillani structures his argument with conditional responses ('if they say... it is said to them...').
The word 'أبوه' may be read as 'أبوا' (they refused). This does not change the argument.
2
Identify the opponent's premise
The opponent claims that the universals (kulliyyat) of the elements are naturally at rest in their centers. Baqillani uses this as a starting point.
3
Follow the parity argument
If the opponent says that the agreement of universals in rest does not prove agreement of nature, Baqillani retorts that similarly, the difference in movements of particulars does not prove difference of nature.
This is a classic dialectical move: the opponent's own standard is applied back to them.
4
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
Baqillani then argues that if the opponent insists on linking movement to nature, then the particulars (which move) must have a different nature from their universals (which are still). This forces the opponent to either accept an absurd conclusion or abandon their position.
The final question about the celestial sphere seals the argument by showing that the same reasoning would deny the unity of nature for all elements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الماء والأرض والنار والهواء لأن من طبع كليات هذه الأشياء الوقوف عالمها الذي هو موضع مركزها وأن لا تتحرك عنه فإن صاروا إلى ذلك تركوا قولهم، وإن قالوا : اتفاق كليات هذه الأشياء في السكون في مراكزها ومواضع كلياتها لا يدل على اتفاق طبعها قيل لهم : وكذلك اختلاف حركات جزئياتها الموجودة في عالمنا لا يدل على اختلاف طباعها ولا فصل في ذلك . ويقال لهم أيضاً: يجب على موضوعكم هذا أن يكون طبع جزئيات هذه الأشياء مخالفاً لكلياتها وأن تكون طباعها خلاف طباع كلياتها؛ وذلك أن من شأن هذه الجزئيات الموجودة في عالمنا الحركة ومن شأن كلياتها السكون والوقوف فيجب لذلك اختلاف طباع الجزئيات والكليات؛ فإن مروا على ذلك تركوا قولهم؛ وإن أبوه قيل لهم : فما أنكرتم أيضاً من اتفاق طبع الفلك والنار والهواء والماء والأرض وإن اختلفت حركات هذه الأمور؟ فلا يجدون إلى دفع ذلك سبيلاً .
Water, earth, fire, and air; because it is in the nature of the universals of these things to be stationary in their place which is the location of their center and not to move from it. If they concede that, they abandon their statement. And if they say: 'The agreement of the universals of these things in rest in their centers and the places of their universals does not indicate the agreement of their nature,' it is said to them: 'Similarly, the difference in the movements of their particulars existing in our world does not indicate a difference in their natures, and there is no distinction in that.' And it is also said to them: 'According to your position, it must be that the nature of the particulars of these things is different from their universals, and that their natures are contrary to the natures of their universals; because the character of these particulars existing in our world is motion, and the character of their universals is rest and stillness, so for that reason the natures of the particulars and universals must differ. If they accept that, they abandon their statement; and if they refuse, it is said to them: 'Then why do you not also deny the agreement of the nature of the celestial sphere, fire, air, water, and earth, even if the movements of these things differ?' So they find no way to refute that.'
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is an argument against an opponent who claims that the natural state of the elements (water, earth, fire, air) proves something about their natures. Baqillani first states the opponent's premise: that the universals (kulliyyat) of these elements are naturally at rest in their respective places (earth at center, etc.) and do not move from them. If the opponent accepts this, their own argument is lost because universals are not in motion. If the opponent then claims that the agreement of universals in rest does not prove agreement of nature, Baqillani turns the argument: similarly, the differing movements of the particulars (juz'iyyat) in our world do not prove differing natures. He then presents a further point: according to the opponent's own logic, the natures of particulars must differ from their universals because particulars move while universals are still; this would force the opponent to abandon their position. If they refuse, Baqillani asks why they do not also deny that the celestial sphere, fire, etc. share a single nature despite their different movements. The opponent is left without a reply.

Key Terms
كليات
جزئيات
طبع
سكون
حركة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The differing movements of the elements (e.g., earth falling, fire rising) prove that they have different natures.
Correction: Baqillani shows that this inference is invalid because it would also require the particulars to have a different nature from their universals, which is absurd. Movement differences alone do not entail nature differences.

Checkpoint
What is the opponent's initial claim about the universals of the elements?
A) They are naturally in motion.
B) They are naturally at rest in their centers.
C) They have no natural place.
D) Their nature is unknown.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's argument shows that the opponent's use of movement to infer nature difference is self-defeating, and that the only consistent position is to accept that all elements share a single nature despite apparent differences in motion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Baqillani shows that outward differences in movement should not lead us to assume different natures. Is there a person or group in your life whose external actions have caused you to judge their 'nature' as fundamentally different from yours? How might this lesson challenge that assumption? Commit today to one specific action that reflects a belief in a shared human nature despite surface differences.
?
If the elements share a single nature despite their diverse motions, what does that imply about the unity underlying all creation? How does this truth affect your sense of connection to the world and to the Creator? Set aside time this week to meditate on the unity of God's creation and how it calls you to greater humility.
?
Baqillani forces his opponent to face the logical consequences of their belief. Is there a belief you hold that, when followed to its logical conclusion, leads to absurdity? Be honest with yourself. What would it cost you to abandon that belief? Ask God for the courage to seek truth even when it is uncomfortable.

Proof of Creation of Celestial Motions from Contradictory States
Baqillani proves celestial motions are created through the impossibility of simultaneous contradictory states.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the impossibility of contradictory states to prove that celestial motions and the bodies themselves are created.

Core Idea
The sun cannot be in two opposite signs at once, so its motion must be created, not eternal.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani presents a logical proof for the creation of celestial bodies' motions. He argues that if the sun's position in each zodiac sign were eternal, it would have to be in multiple contradictory positions simultaneously. This impossibility demonstrates that the motion is created, and since the bodies never exist without these states, the bodies themselves must be created as well.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Try to grasp the overall argument before diving into details.
The passage is dense; reading it aloud may help.
2
Understand the key concept of contradictory states
Baqillani argues that the sun's being in one zodiac sign (e.g., Aries) contradicts its being in another (e.g., Taurus) at the same time. This contradiction is impossible.
Think of it like a person being in two rooms at once – it's logically impossible.
3
Follow the logical chain
If the sun's positions were eternal, then it would have to be in all signs simultaneously (since eternal means always present). That would force contradictory states, which is impossible. Therefore, the motion cannot be eternal and must be created.
The argument uses a reductio ad absurdum: assuming eternal leads to an impossibility, so the assumption is false.
4
Connect to the creation of the spheres themselves
Baqillani extends the argument: since the celestial spheres never exist without these created motions, the spheres themselves must be created as well.
This is a powerful inference: if a thing is always accompanied by created properties, the thing itself is created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في من كل برج إلى غيره وأن كونها فيه مضاد لكونها في غيره دليل أنه لا يجوز أن يكون كونها في هذه البروج قديماً لأن ذلك لو كان كذلك لوجب أن تكون في برج الحمل في حال كونها في برج الثور ولم تكن بأن تكون أحد المكانين بأولى من أن تكون في الآخر إذا كان كونها فيهما قديماً لم يزل موجوداً ولا يزال كذلك موجوداً وإذا لم يجز ذلك ثبت حدوث حركات هذه الأفلاك وأكوانها وثبت بذلك حدوثها لأنها عندنا وعندهم لم توجد قط من هذه الأكوان ; وما لم يسبق الحوادث فواجب كونه محدثاً. وقد من قبل قول من زعم أن الحوادث لا أول لها بما يغني عن رده ; فوجب القضاء على حدوث هذه الأجسام
That from each sign to another, and that its being in it is contradictory to its being in another, is evidence that it is not permissible for its being in these signs to be eternal. Because if that were so, it would be necessary for it to be in the sign of Aries while being in the sign of Taurus, and it would not be more appropriate for it to be in one of the two places than the other, if its being in both were eternal, never ceasing to exist and always existing. And when that is not permissible, the creation of the motions of these celestial spheres and their states is established, and thereby their creation is established, because according to us and them it never existed apart from these states; and whatever is not preceded by events is necessarily created. And we have previously refuted the claim of those who assert that events have no beginning with what suffices from its refutation; so judgment is necessitated on the creation of these bodies.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the creation of celestial motions. The author argues that if the sun's position in each zodiac sign were eternal, then it would have to be in two different signs at once, which is impossible. Therefore, the motions must be created. He then concludes that the bodies themselves are created since they never exist without these states. He also references a prior refutation of those who claim events have no beginning.

Key Terms
برج
كون
قديم
محدث
حادث
حركات أفلاك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument only works if the sun moves through discrete signs, but it applies to any body with successive states.
Correction: The logic of contradictory states applies to any entity that undergoes change: if its state at one moment is eternal, it would have to be in contradictory states simultaneously, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani use as evidence that the motions of celestial bodies are not eternal?
A) That the sun's being in one sign contradicts its being in another simultaneously, proving temporality.
B) That the planets have no actual influence on earthly events.
C) That the celestial spheres are composed of simple elements.
D) That the seasons change regularly.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of a body being in two contradictory states at once proves that its motion is created, not eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof shows that even the sun's motion cannot be eternal—it must have a beginning. What does this imply about your own daily routines and habits? Are there areas of your life where you act as if they will last forever, ignoring the truth that everything created is temporary? Commit to one change today that reflects your belief in the transience of this world.
?
Baqillani uses logical necessity to prove creation. Do you believe in Allah's existence based on such reasoned certainty, or have you simply inherited faith? If you are honest, do you ever entertain doubts? What would it take for you to personally demonstrate to yourself the logical necessity of a Creator? Resolve to study one proof seriously this week.
?
If the celestial spheres themselves are created and dependent, then every stable thing you rely on—your health, relationships, wealth—is also created and contingent. Which of these do you unconsciously treat as eternal in your heart? Confess that attachment to Allah and ask Him to make you see all things as His fleeting gifts.

Second Proof: Capability or Incapability of Planets
Baqillani presents a second proof that planets cannot cause effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's second proof that planets cannot cause earthly and celestial events, based on the logical dichotomy of capability or incapability.

Core Idea
Planets cannot cause effects because they either lack capability or would conflict with each other.

Baqillani continues his refutation of astrological causation with a second proof, based on a logical dichotomy. He analyzes whether planets are capable of producing effects or not. This argument reinforces the Ash'ari position that only God is the true agent of all events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the English translation. Notice the structure of the argument: a conditional statement followed by two branches.
The passage is incomplete due to a page break, but the core argument is clear.
2
Follow the dichotomy
Identify the two possibilities: the planets are either capable of causing effects or not. For each branch, observe the conclusion Baqillani draws.
If not capable, actions are impossible. If capable, each planet could prevent the others, leading to conflict.
3
Reflect on the refutation
Consider how this argument undermines the idea that planets can be independent agents. Why does the possibility of conflict show they cannot be the true causes?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يدل أيضاً على أنه لا يجوز أن تكون هذه التأثيرات والحوادث الأرضية والسماوية من فعل هذه الكواكب أنها لو كانت من فعلها لم تخل أن تكون فعلت هذه الأمور، وهي قادرة عليها أو غير قادرة على ذلك؛ فإن كانت غير قادرة على ذلك استحال وقوع الأفعال منها كما يستحيل وقوع القصد والاختيار وحل الأشكال وعمل الهندسة ودقائق الكتابة والنساجة والزرع والمساحة عندهم وعندنا ممن ليس بقادر وذلك لأن الفعل إنما تعلق بفاعل حي قادر من حيث كان فعلاً فإذا جاز وقوع بعض الأفعال من غير قادر خرج جميعها عن الحاجة إلى التعلق بقادر ; وفي بطلان ذلك دليل على أنها لا تجوز أن تكون غير قادرة. وإن كانت قادرة على ما كان منها ومختارة له فلا يخلو كل واحدة منها، قديمة كانت أو محدثة، من أن يكون قادراً على ممانعة الآخر من فعله والاستبداد بوجود مراده دون مراد
And what also indicates that it is not permissible for these effects and earthly and celestial events to be from the action of these planets is that if they were from their action, they would not be free from having done these things while being capable of them or not capable of that. If they are not capable of that, then the occurrence of actions from them is impossible, just as the occurrence of intent and choice, solving geometrical problems, doing engineering, intricacies of writing, weaving, agriculture, and surveying is impossible, according to them and us, from one who is not capable. That is because action is attached to a living, capable agent insofar as it is an action; so if the occurrence of some actions from one who is not capable is permitted, all actions would exit from the need to be attached to a capable agent. And the invalidity of that is evidence that they cannot be not capable. And if they are capable of what occurs from them and choose it, then each one of them, whether eternal or created, is not free from being capable of preventing the other from its action and of being independent in realizing its own desire without the desire of the other.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This is a second proof against astrological causation. It presents a dichotomy: either the planets are capable of causing effects or not. If not, actions cannot occur from them because action requires a capable agent. If they are capable, then each planet would be able to prevent the others' effects, leading to conflict and inconsistency. The text cuts off, but the argument is that such conflict would show that the effects cannot be consistently attributed to the planets.

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
5 min
The Dilemma of Planetary Capability
Baqillani presents a dilemma about planetary capability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's initial argument that either planets are incapable of preventing effects, implying deficiency, or their Maker is the true agent, proving all events are from a single capable, choosing Creator.

Core Idea
Planets cannot be independent causes; either they are weak or the Creator is the sole agent.

Baqillani opens with a dilemma that cuts to the heart of astrological causation. He forces the astrologer to choose: either the planet has no power to prevent its supposed effects, or it does. If it lacks power, it is deficient and contingent; if it has power, then its Maker must be the real cause. This argument establishes that all events in the world are directly from God, not from celestial bodies.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma carefully
Notice how Baqillani presents two mutually exclusive options regarding the planet's ability to prevent effects. Trace the logical consequence of each option.
The passage assumes the sun in Taurus as an example from astrology.
2
Analyze the first option
If the planet is not capable of preventing the effects, then it is overcome by the celestial spheres, which implies deficiency and contingency in the planet. Ask: why would deficiency prove the planet is created?
3
Analyze the second option
If the planet is capable, then the true agent is the Maker who can prevent these effects or create others. This means the planets have no necessary causal role.
Baqillani's conclusion: all is the act of a capable, choosing Agent.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The dilemma leads to the same result: planets are not independent causes. All events are from a single Creator who acts as He wills.
This sets the stage for the next proof (mutual hindrance).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
برج وجب قادراً على ألا تكون الحوادث التي يوجبون وجودها عند كون الشمس في الثور ومقابلتها لما قابلته أو غير قادر على ذلك فإن كان غير قادر عليه ممانعة هذه الأفلاك له وغلبتها إياه وذلك يقتضي نقصه وحدوثه وإن كان صانعها قادراً على المنع من وجود هذه التأثيرات مع وجود الأفلاك ومقابلتها وتربيعها وتسديسها وثبوت طبائعها ويقدر على إيجاد غيرها من الحوادث بطل أن تكون لهذه الكواكب أفعال وتأثير وطباع توجب حدوث ما يحدث في عالمنا وثبت أن ذلك أجمع فعلُ فاعل قادر مختار يُحدثه إذا شاء ويتركه إذا شاء .
ومما يدل أيضاً على أنه لا يجوز أن تكون هذه التأثيرات والحوادث الأرضية والسماوية من فعل هذه الكواكب أنها لو كانت من فعلها لم تخلُ أن تكون فعلت هذه الأمور، وهي قادرة عليها أو غير قادرة على ذلك؛ فإن كانت غير قادرة على ذلك استحال وقوع الأفعال منها كما يستحيل وقوع القصد والاختيار وحل الأشكال وعمل الهندسة ودقائق الكتابة والنساجة والزرع والمساحة عندهم وعندنا ممن ليس بقادر وذلك لأن الفعل إنما تعلق بفاعل حي قادر من حيث كان فعلاً فإذا جاز وقوع بعض الأفعال من غير قادر خرج جميعها عن الحاجة إلى التعلق بقادر؛ وفي بطلان ذلك دليل على أنها لا تجوز أن تكون غير قادرة. وإن كانت قادرة على ما كان منها ومختارة له فلا يخلو كل واحدة منها، قديمة كانت أو محدثة، من أن يكون قادراً على ممانعة الآخر من فعله والاستبداد بوجود مراده دون مراد مخالفه، أو لا يكون فيها قادراً على ذلك، أو يكون بعضها قادراً على هذا وبعضه غير قادر عليه؛ ويساق معهم دليل التمانع بعينه، فإنه مفسد لقولهم وموجب لحدوث سائر هذه الأفلاك وفيه ترك تدينهم بقدمها.
فأما من قال من المنجمين إن هذه الكواكب مُحْدَثَةٌ وأنها حيةٌ قادرةٌ قاصدة فإنه جوز تمانُعَها ولحوق العجز بها فإنهم لا سبيل لهم إلى العلم بكونها قادرة مختارة؛ وما معهم فيه سوى الدعوى؛ فيقال لهم : لم قلتم إن هذه الأفلاك حية قادرة؟ فإن قالوا : لظهور ما ظهر من سيرها وقطعها البروج وكونها فيها على ترتيب ونظام وفي الأوقات المعلومة، قيل لهم : وما الدليل على أن هذه الحركات من فعلها وأنها قادرة عليها مع علمنا وإياكم بأنه قد يتحرك الحي والميت والقادر ومن ليس بقادر فما في ظهور الحركات منها ما يدل على أنها قادرة؟ وما أنكرتم أن يكون صانعها خالقاً للسير وقطع البروج فيها؟ . فإن قالوا : الذي به نعلم أن ما يظهر من حركات الناس وتصرفهم فعل لهم به نعلم أن سیر هذه الكواكب وكونها في البروج فعل لها؛ يقال لهم : لم قلتم ذلك؟ وما أنكرتم أن يكون علم الإنسان بأن نفسه فاعلة لقيامه وقعــوده وضروب تصرُّفه المتعلق بقدرته هو وجوده لنفسه قادرة على ذلك ومختارة له ، وعلى خلاف صفته إذا دفع وسُحب واضطر إلى حركة مثل حركة الحمى والفالج ، وأن يكون علمه بأن غيره من الناس المتصرفين في الصياغة والكتابة مختارون لذلك وقاصدون إليه وقادرون عليه، يقع اضطراراً من وجه يلزم النفس العلمُ به؛ لأننا قد نضطر إلى علم كون
And it is necessary that he is capable of not creating the events that they assert occur when the sun is in Taurus and in opposition to what it opposes, or he is not capable of that. If he is not capable of preventing them, then these celestial spheres overcome and dominate him, and that necessitates his deficiency and contingency. And if their Maker is capable of preventing the existence of these effects with the existence of the celestial spheres, their oppositions, quadrants, sextiles, and the persistence of their natures, and He is able to create other events, then it becomes false that these planets have actions, effects, and natures that necessitate the occurrence of what occurs in our world, and it is established that all of that is the act of a capable, choosing Agent who brings it into existence when He wills and leaves it when He wills.
Also among the proofs that it is not permissible for these effects and earthly and heavenly events to be from the action of these planets is that if they were from their action, they would not be free from either being capable of these things or not being capable of that. If they were not capable of that, then the occurrence of actions from them would be impossible, just as it is impossible for intention, choice, solving geometrical problems, doing engineering, the subtleties of writing, weaving, planting, and surveying to occur from one who is not capable, according to them and according to us. That is because an action is only connected to a living, capable agent inasmuch as it is an action. If the occurrence of some actions from one who is not capable were permissible, then all actions would be exempt from the need to be connected to a capable agent. And in the falsehood of that is proof that they cannot be not capable. And if they are capable of what occurs from them and are choosing for it, then each one of them, whether ancient or originated, can only be such that it is capable of preventing the other from its action and being independent in bringing about its own desire instead of the desire of its opponent, or none of them is capable of that, or some of them are capable of this and some are not capable of it. And the proof of mutual hindrance (dalīl al-tamānuʿ) is brought against them exactly, for it invalidates their statement and necessitates the origination of all these celestial spheres, and in it is abandonment of their belief in their eternity.
As for those astrologers who say that these planets are originated and that they are alive, capable, and intending, then he has allowed their mutual hindrance and the occurrence of incapacity in them, but they have no way to know that they are capable and choosing; they have nothing but mere claims. So it is said to them: Why do you claim that these celestial spheres are alive and capable? If they say: Because of the appearance of their motion, their traversing the zodiac signs, and their being in them in an ordered and systematic manner at known times, it is said to them: What is the proof that these motions are from their action and that they are capable of them, given that we and you know that the living, the dead, the capable, and the one who is not capable can move? So there is nothing in the appearance of motions that indicates they are capable. And why do you not accept that their Maker is the Creator of their motion and traversing of the zodiac signs in them? If they say: That by which we know that what appears from people's motions and conduct is their action—by it we know that the motion of these planets and their being in the zodiac signs is their action. It is said to them: Why do you say that? And why do you not accept that a person's knowledge that he himself is an agent in his standing, sitting, and various actions connected to his power is his existence for himself as capable of that and choosing it, as opposed to his state when he is pushed, dragged, and forced into a motion like the motion of fever and palsy? And that his knowledge that other people are acting in craftsmanship and writing are choosing for that, intending it, and capable of it, occurs necessarily from an aspect that obligates the soul's knowledge of it, because we are compelled to the knowledge of the existence...
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a sustained refutation of astrological causation. The author, Imam Baqillani, presents a series of logical arguments to disprove the claim that planets produce effects in the sublunary world.

The passage begins with a dilemma already in progress (likely continued from a previous page): either the planet is capable of preventing the effects that astrologers claim occur when the sun is in certain positions, or it is not. If it is not capable, then it is overcome and subjugated by the celestial spheres, which implies deficiency and contingency in the planet. If it is capable, then the true agent is the Maker who can prevent these effects and create others—proving that the planets have no necessary causal role, but all is from a capable, choosing Creator.

Next, Baqillani introduces another proof: if planetary effects existed, the planets must be capable of producing them. If they were not capable, then actions would occur from the incapable, which is absurd—actions require a living, capable agent. If they are capable, then each planet must either be able to prevent the others' actions or not. This leads directly to the proof of mutual hindrance (dalīl al-tamānuʿ), which shows that if multiple independent agents existed, they would conflict, requiring either one to overcome the others or all to be contingent, thus proving the planets are originated and not eternal.

Finally, Baqillani addresses a subgroup of astrologers who claim planets are created, alive, and capable. He challenges their evidence: the regular motion of planets does not prove they are agents, since motion can occur from inanimate forces. The analogy with human voluntary actions fails because human knowledge of agency is immediate and self-evident, not derived from observing motion alone. The passage cuts off while explaining the nature of this necessary knowledge.

Key Terms
كواكب
قادر
مختار
فاعل
حوداث

B) It is deficient and contingent.
C) It is the true cause of events.
D) It is indifferent to the effects.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's dilemma forces the conclusion that planets are not independent causes; all events originate from a single capable and choosing Creator.

The Proof of Mutual Hindrance Against Planets
Baqillani applies the proof of mutual hindrance to planets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's application of the proof of mutual hindrance (dalīl al-tamānuʿ) to refute the idea that planets are independent agents, and how it demonstrates their contingency and createdness.

Core Idea
Multiple independent agents would conflict, proving planets cannot be gods or eternal causes.

Baqillani now introduces a classic kalam argument against multiple deities: the proof of mutual hindrance. He applies it to the celestial spheres, arguing that if planets were capable and choosing agents, they would either conflict or be unable to act independently. This leads to the conclusion that the spheres must be created and not eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the second argument
Notice how Baqillani builds on the initial dilemma. He now assumes planets are capable and choosing, then draws out the consequences.
This argument is structured as a conditional: if planets were capable agents, then...
2
Identify the three scenarios
Baqillani lists three possibilities: each planet can prevent the others, none can, or some can. He then applies the proof of mutual hindrance to show all lead to absurdity.
The proof of mutual hindrance (dalīl al-tamānuʿ) is a standard kalam argument against multiple gods.
3
Understand the conclusion
The proof invalidates the astrologers' claim and necessitates that the celestial spheres are originated (created), contradicting the belief in their eternity.
Baqillani says: 'it invalidates their statement and necessitates the origination of all these celestial spheres'.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
This argument shows that even if planets were capable agents, they cannot be eternal or independent. Only one Creator can be the source of all events.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some astrologers think that multiple planetary agents can coexist without conflict.

Checkpoint
What does the proof of mutual hindrance (dalīl al-tamānuʿ) entail for the celestial spheres according to Baqillani?

C) It shows they are capable of harmony.
D) It confirms their independence.

Key Takeaway
The proof of mutual hindrance demonstrates that multiple independent planetary agents are impossible, leading to the conclusion that the celestial spheres are created and not eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What 'planets' have you set up as independent causes in your life — people, circumstances, or habits — that you treat as though they have power independent of Allah? How would this proof dismantle that assumption in your heart?
?
Do you ever find yourself trying to assert your will over others, as if you were an independent agent? How does the proof of mutual hindrance expose the futility of that struggle and call you to submit to the sole Agent?
?
If the celestial spheres cannot be eternal because they would mutually hinder, what does that say about the idols of permanence you cling to — careers, relationships, or reputations? Will you let this truth uproot them today?

Refuting the Claim of Living, Capable Planets
Baqillani refutes the claim that planets are living agents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's refutation of astrologers who claim that planets are created, alive, and capable agents, and why regular motion does not prove agency.

Core Idea
Regular motion does not imply agency; only direct experience of one's own volition proves capability.

Baqillani now addresses a specific group of astrologers who concede that planets are created but maintain they are living, capable, and intentional. He challenges their evidence, arguing that the regular motion of planets does not prove they are agents, since motion can occur from inanimate forces. He then begins to discuss how humans know their own agency, drawing a distinction between voluntary and forced motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the third argument
This passage targets a more refined astrological view. Notice that Baqillani first states their claim, then demands proof.
The passage cuts off mid-sentence at the end of the chunk.
2
Identify the astrologers' evidence
They cite the regular motion of planets and their orderly traversal of zodiac signs as proof of life, capability, and intention.
Baqillani questions whether motion alone is sufficient evidence.
3
Understand Baqillani's counter
He points out that motion can occur from the living and the dead, the capable and the incapable. So regular motion does not prove that the planet is an agent.
He also suggests that the Maker could be the one producing the motion.
4
Follow the analogy with human action
Baqillani begins to compare the knowledge of human agency: we know our own actions are voluntary by direct experience, and we know others' actions by necessity. The passage ends during this explanation.
Though incomplete, the argument is clear: the astrologers' analogy fails.

برج وجب قادراً على ألا تكون الحوادث التي يوجبون وجودها عند كون الشمس في الثور ومقابلتها لما قابلته أو غير قادر على ذلك فإن كان غير قادر عليه ممانعة هذه الأفلاك له وغلبتها إياه وذلك يقتضي نقصه وحدوثه وإن كان صانعها قادراً على المنع من وجود هذه التأثيرات مع وجود الأفلاك ومقابلتها وتربيعها وتسديسها وثبوت طبائعها ويقدر على إيجاد غيرها من الحوادث بطل أن تكون لهذه الكواكب أفعال وتأثير وطباع توجب حدوث ما يحدث في عالمنا وثبت أن ذلك أجمع فعلُ فاعل قادر مختار يُحدثه إذا شاء ويتركه إذا شاء .
ومما يدل أيضاً على أنه لا يجوز أن تكون هذه التأثيرات والحوادث الأرضية والسماوية من فعل هذه الكواكب أنها لو كانت من فعلها لم تخلُ أن تكون فعلت هذه الأمور، وهي قادرة عليها أو غير قادرة على ذلك؛ فإن كانت غير قادرة على ذلك استحال وقوع الأفعال منها كما يستحيل وقوع القصد والاختيار وحل الأشكال وعمل الهندسة ودقائق الكتابة والنساجة والزرع والمساحة عندهم وعندنا ممن ليس بقادر وذلك لأن الفعل إنما تعلق بفاعل حي قادر من حيث كان فعلاً فإذا جاز وقوع بعض الأفعال من غير قادر خرج جميعها عن الحاجة إلى التعلق بقادر؛ وفي بطلان ذلك دليل على أنها لا تجوز أن تكون غير قادرة. وإن كانت قادرة على ما كان منها ومختارة له فلا يخلو كل واحدة منها، قديمة كانت أو محدثة، من أن يكون قادراً على ممانعة الآخر من فعله والاستبداد بوجود مراده دون مراد مخالفه، أو لا يكون فيها قادراً على ذلك، أو يكون بعضها قادراً على هذا وبعضه غير قادر عليه؛ ويساق معهم دليل التمانع بعينه، فإنه مفسد لقولهم وموجب لحدوث سائر هذه الأفلاك وفيه ترك تدينهم بقدمها.
فأما من قال من المنجمين إن هذه الكواكب مُحْدَثَةٌ وأنها حيةٌ قادرةٌ قاصدة فإنه جوز تمانُعَها ولحوق العجز بها فإنهم لا سبيل لهم إلى العلم بكونها قادرة مختارة؛ وما معهم فيه سوى الدعوى؛ فيقال لهم : لم قلتم إن هذه الأفلاك حية قادرة؟ فإن قالوا : لظهور ما ظهر من سيرها وقطعها البروج وكونها فيها على ترتيب ونظام وفي الأوقات المعلومة، قيل لهم : وما الدليل على أن هذه الحركات من فعلها وأنها قادرة عليها مع علمنا وإياكم بأنه قد يتحرك الحي والميت والقادر ومن ليس بقادر فما في ظهور الحركات منها ما يدل على أنها قادرة؟ وما أنكرتم أن يكون صانعها خالقاً للسير وقطع البروج فيها؟ . فإن قالوا : الذي به نعلم أن ما يظهر من حركات الناس وتصرفهم فعل لهم به نعلم أن سیر هذه الكواكب وكونها في البروج فعل لها؛ يقال لهم : لم قلتم ذلك؟ وما أنكرتم أن يكون علم الإنسان بأن نفسه فاعلة لقيامه وقعــوده وضروب تصرُّفه المتعلق بقدرته هو وجوده لنفسه قادرة على ذلك ومختارة له ، وعلى خلاف صفته إذا دفع وسُحب واضطر إلى حركة مثل حركة الحمى والفالج ، وأن يكون علمه بأن غيره من الناس المتصرفين في الصياغة والكتابة مختارون لذلك وقاصدون إليه وقادرون عليه، يقع اضطراراً من وجه يلزم النفس العلمُ به؛ لأننا قد نضطر إلى علم كون
And it is necessary that he is capable of not creating the events that they assert occur when the sun is in Taurus and in opposition to what it opposes, or he is not capable of that. If he is not capable of preventing them, then these celestial spheres overcome and dominate him, and that necessitates his deficiency and contingency. And if their Maker is capable of preventing the existence of these effects with the existence of the celestial spheres, their oppositions, quadrants, sextiles, and the persistence of their natures, and He is able to create other events, then it becomes false that these planets have actions, effects, and natures that necessitate the occurrence of what occurs in our world, and it is established that all of that is the act of a capable, choosing Agent who brings it into existence when He wills and leaves it when He wills.
Also among the proofs that it is not permissible for these effects and earthly and heavenly events to be from the action of these planets is that if they were from their action, they would not be free from either being capable of these things or not being capable of that. If they were not capable of that, then the occurrence of actions from them would be impossible, just as it is impossible for intention, choice, solving geometrical problems, doing engineering, the subtleties of writing, weaving, planting, and surveying to occur from one who is not capable, according to them and according to us. That is because an action is only connected to a living, capable agent inasmuch as it is an action. If the occurrence of some actions from one who is not capable were permissible, then all actions would be exempt from the need to be connected to a capable agent. And in the falsehood of that is proof that they cannot be not capable. And if they are capable of what occurs from them and are choosing for it, then each one of them, whether ancient or originated, can only be such that it is capable of preventing the other from its action and being independent in bringing about its own desire instead of the desire of its opponent, or none of them is capable of that, or some of them are capable of this and some are not capable of it. And the proof of mutual hindrance (dalīl al-tamānuʿ) is brought against them exactly, for it invalidates their statement and necessitates the origination of all these celestial spheres, and in it is abandonment of their belief in their eternity.
As for those astrologers who say that these planets are originated and that they are alive, capable, and intending, then he has allowed their mutual hindrance and the occurrence of incapacity in them, but they have no way to know that they are capable and choosing; they have nothing but mere claims. So it is said to them: Why do you claim that these celestial spheres are alive and capable? If they say: Because of the appearance of their motion, their traversing the zodiac signs, and their being in them in an ordered and systematic manner at known times, it is said to them: What is the proof that these motions are from their action and that they are capable of them, given that we and you know that the living, the dead, the capable, and the one who is not capable can move? So there is nothing in the appearance of motions that indicates they are capable. And why do you not accept that their Maker is the Creator of their motion and traversing of the zodiac signs in them? If they say: That by which we know that what appears from people's motions and conduct is their action—by it we know that the motion of these planets and their being in the zodiac signs is their action. It is said to them: Why do you say that? And why do you not accept that a person's knowledge that he himself is an agent in his standing, sitting, and various actions connected to his power is his existence for himself as capable of that and choosing it, as opposed to his state when he is pushed, dragged, and forced into a motion like the motion of fever and palsy? And that his knowledge that other people are acting in craftsmanship and writing are choosing for that, intending it, and capable of it, occurs necessarily from an aspect that obligates the soul's knowledge of it, because we are compelled to the knowledge of the existence...
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a sustained refutation of astrological causation. The author, Imam Baqillani, presents a series of logical arguments to disprove the claim that planets produce effects in the sublunary world.

The passage begins with a dilemma already in progress (likely continued from a previous page): either the planet is capable of preventing the effects that astrologers claim occur when the sun is in certain positions, or it is not. If it is not capable, then it is overcome and subjugated by the celestial spheres, which implies deficiency and contingency in the planet. If it is capable, then the true agent is the Maker who can prevent these effects and create others—proving that the planets have no necessary causal role, but all is from a capable, choosing Creator.

Next, Baqillani introduces another proof: if planetary effects existed, the planets must be capable of producing them. If they were not capable, then actions would occur from the incapable, which is absurd—actions require a living, capable agent. If they are capable, then each planet must either be able to prevent the others' actions or not. This leads directly to the proof of mutual hindrance (dalīl al-tamānuʿ), which shows that if multiple independent agents existed, they would conflict, requiring either one to overcome the others or all to be contingent, thus proving the planets are originated and not eternal.

Finally, Baqillani addresses a subgroup of astrologers who claim planets are created, alive, and capable. He challenges their evidence: the regular motion of planets does not prove they are agents, since motion can occur from inanimate forces. The analogy with human voluntary actions fails because human knowledge of agency is immediate and self-evident, not derived from observing motion alone. The passage cuts off while explaining the nature of this necessary knowledge.

Correction: Baqillani shows that motion alone is insufficient evidence; it could be caused by an external force.

Key Takeaway
Regular celestial motion does not prove that planets are living, capable agents; the true cause is the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the order and intricacy of the universe—the sunrise, the seasons, the stars—do you ever find yourself attributing that order to the objects themselves, as if they possess their own capability? How does Baqillani's argument strip away that illusion and demand you redirect your awe exclusively to the Creator? Will you today, during your next prayer, consciously praise Allah as the sole origin of every motion you see?
?
The astrologers saw regularity and concluded the planets themselves were agents. In your own life, when you see consistent outcomes—success in work, health, relationships—are you tempted to attribute them to your own capability, your planning, your effort? Where is the line between gratitude and self-congratulation? Baqillani reminds you that even your own standing and sitting are not ultimately from you. Is there an area of your life where you still cling to the illusion of self-sufficiency? What will you do tonight to break that pride?

Is there a single decision you made today that you forgot to submit to His will? The passage calls you to acknowledge that even your voluntary actions are encompassed by His power. Will you, right now, repent for any moment you felt independent of Him and commit to saying 'Allah willing' before your next action?

Objection: Uniform Motion Suggests Compulsion, Not Free Will
Baqillani presents and evaluates the objection that uniform stellar motion indicates compulsion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani evaluates the objection that the uniform motion of stars indicates compulsion by nature rather than free will.

Core Idea
Uniform motion can suggest compulsion, not intelligence.

In this passage, Baqillani presents an objection from opponents of free will in celestial bodies. The objector argues that the constant, uniform motion of stars is more characteristic of a compelled nature than of a voluntary agent. Baqillani acknowledges the plausibility of this objection, comparing it to natural effects like fire and snow.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice how the objector argues that uniform motion indicates compulsion.
The word 'طباع' (natures) is key.
2
Identify Baqillani's response
Baqillani does not reject the objection; he says it is 'closer' to the truth. Understand why.
He compares stars' effects to fire and snow.
3
Contrast voluntary vs compelled action
A voluntary agent can do opposites; a compelled nature acts uniformly. See the distinction in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى أنه لو قال قائل: إن ما يظهر من حركات النجوم وسيرها ودوران الفلك على نمط واحد وسجية واحدة غير مختلفة يدل على أنها مجبولة على ذلك، ومضطرة إليه، ومطبوعة عليه على قول أصحاب الطباع، لكان ذلك أقرب لأن المطبوع المجبول على الفعل من شأنه أن يكون ما يضطر إليه على سجية واحدة وليس كذلك المتصرف باختياره لأنه يفعل الشيء وضده وخلافه، فتأثيرات هذه النجوم لما تؤثره على سنن واحد يجري مجرى تأثير النار والثلج للتسخين والتبريد على سجية واحدة وتأثير الطعام والشراب وما جرى مجرى ذلك فما ظهر من حركاتها أقرب إلى أن يدل على قول أصحاب الطباع.
And further, if someone were to say: What appears of the motions of the stars, their course, and the rotation of the sphere on a single pattern and a single nature, not differing, indicates that they are impelled to that, forced to it, and imprinted upon it according to the proponents of natural dispositions (tabāʾiʿ), then that would be closer, because the imprinted and impelled to action is such that what he is forced to is on a single nature, but the one who acts by his choice is not like that, because he does a thing and its opposite and its contrary. So the effects of these stars, since they produce effects on a single course, run in the manner of the effect of fire and snow for heating and cooling on a single nature, and the effect of food and drink and what runs in that course. So what appears of their motions is closer to indicating the proponents of natural dispositions.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage presents a hypothetical objection to the astrologers' claim that stars are voluntary agents. The objector says that the constant, uniform motion of the stars—always the same pattern—actually suggests that they are compelled by their nature (ṭabʿ) rather than acting by choice. A voluntary agent can act differently, but these motions never vary. Baqillani acknowledges that this objection has some merit: the uniformity of stellar motion is more consistent with the view of those who believe in innate natures (aṣḥāb al-ṭabāʾiʿ) than with the claim of free will. He compares the stars' effects to the constant effects of fire (heating) and snow (cooling), which are uniform by nature, not by choice.

?
The objector argues that a voluntary agent can act contrary to their usual pattern. When was the last time you did something truly contrary to your nature—not out of compulsion, but as a conscious act of faith? If you cannot remember, what does that suggest about your spiritual freedom?

Analogy between Human and Celestial Actions
The author argues that human action analogy does not prove stars are living.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the observable movements of stars do not count as evidence that they are living, capable beings, based on the distinction between customary association and causal inference.

Core Idea
Customary association is not causal proof of life in the stars.

In this lesson, Imam al-Baqillani tackles a claim that the stars must be alive because they move in purposeful ways. He uses an analogy with human actions to show that mere observation of regular behavior does not necessarily imply intrinsic agency. The passage establishes that our knowledge of human intentionality comes from custom, not from direct causal inference, and the same reasoning prevents us from deducing life in celestial bodies.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation carefully. Notice how the author builds his argument by first discussing human actions.
The passage uses a compressed style; pay attention to the key terms like 'custom' and 'compelled'.
2
Identify the two analogies
The author presents two analogies: one about voluntary human actions (willing, intending) and another about emotional states (bashfulness, fear). In both cases, our knowledge comes from custom, not from observing the cause.
Contrast the direct causation view with the customary association view.
3
Understand the conclusion
The author applies the same logic to the stars: we have no customary knowledge linking their motions to life, and no evidence (dalīl) for inference. Therefore, we cannot know they are living.
This conclusion refutes astrological claims of stellar agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المريد منا مريداً والقاصد قاصداً وأنه بالصفة التي إذا كنا نحن عليها سُمِّينـا قادرين، عند أحوال تظهر منهم ليست بأسباب لكونهم قادرين ولا دالة على ذلك، ولكنا نُضطر عند مشاهدتها والعلم بها إلى كونهم قاصدين وأنهم بصفة القادرين على سبيل وضع العادة ومُسْتَقَرَّها ؛ كما نضطر إلى خَجَل الخجل ووَجَل الوَجل وشجاعة الشجاع أو جبن الجبان عند أمور تظهر منهم ليست بأسباب الشجاعة والجبن ولا دالةً عليها؛ ولكن العادة جارية بحصول العلم الضروري بأحوالهم عند حصولها وإذا كان ذلك كذلك، ولم نكن مضطرين إلى العلم بأن النجوم مختارة قادرة حية ولا عالمين بذلك من جهة الاستدلال لفقد الدليل عليه ثبت أنه لا سبيل لهم إلى العلم بأنها حية قادرة.
The one who wills among us is willing, and the one who intends is intending, and that he is with the attribute by which, when we are upon it, we are called capable, upon states that appear from them that are not causes for their being capable nor indicative of that. But we are compelled at witnessing them and knowing them to their being intending and that they are with the attribute of the capable, by way of the establishment of custom and its stability, just as we are compelled to the bashfulness of the bashful, the fear of the fearful, the bravery of the brave, or the cowardice of the coward, upon matters that appear from them that are not causes of bravery and cowardice nor indicative of them. Rather, custom continues upon the occurrence of necessary knowledge of their states upon their occurrence. And if that is so, and we are not compelled to the knowledge that the stars are choosing, capable, living, nor are we knowers of that by way of inference due to the lack of evidence for it, it is established that there is no way for them to the knowledge that they are living, capable.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage presents an argument by analogy to refute the claim that the stars are living and capable agents. The author describes how we perceive human intentional actions: we see a person acting in a certain way and are compelled by habit (al-‘āda) to know that they are willing and capable, even though those observable actions are not the true causes of their ability. Similarly, we are compelled to know emotional states like bashfulness or courage from observable behaviors, again by customary association. The author then applies this to the celestial realm: if we observe the motions of the stars, we are not compelled by any inner necessity to know that they are living, choosing agents, nor can we deduce this by rational inference because there is no evidence (dalīl) for it. Therefore, the astrologers have no basis for claiming that the stars are alive and powerful.

Key Terms
عادة
اضطرار
علم ضروري
استدلال
دليل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the analogy implies human voluntary actions are directly caused by observable behaviors.
Correction: The author distinguishes between cause and customary association; we are compelled to know by custom, not because the behavior is a cause.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say we cannot know the stars are living by inference?
A) Because the stars do not move by choice.
B) Because there is no evidence (dalīl) for it.
C) Because the stars are too far away.
D) Because we are compelled to know they are not living.

Key Takeaway
The lack of a reliable customary connection and the absence of evidence (dalīl) prevent us from inferring that the stars are living, capable beings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe someone's behavior and assume you know their intentions, how often do you forget that this knowledge is merely customary, not certain? Will you pause today to question a judgment you made about someone's motives, acknowledging your reliance on habit rather than true knowledge?
?
If you saw a shooting star, would you suppose it has a purpose or will? What if you saw a pattern in natural events and felt they were directed? How might this lesson change your habitual attribution of agency to things you observe? Will you consciously remind yourself that without dalīl, such attributions are baseless?
?
Think of a time you were certain about someone's character from their actions, only to be proven wrong. Did that shake your trust in customary knowledge? This passage says such knowledge is not causal, just habitual. Will you live today with the humility that your judgments are not necessary truths, but mere customs (ʿādāt)?

Uniform Motion and Compulsion: Examining the First Objection
First part of a two-part refutation: the objection that uniform motion proves compulsion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first objection that stars' uniform motion implies they are compelled by nature, and how the author turns this objection on its head.

Core Idea
Uniform motion suggests compulsion, not free will.

Imam al-Baqillani presents a hypothetical objection from astrologers who argue that the celestial bodies' regular, unvarying motions indicate they are compelled by nature, not acting by choice. He then shows that this argument actually supports the proponents of 'nature' (tab‘) rather than free choice, because compelled things act uniformly while voluntary agents can do opposites. Let's examine this argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the structure: first the objection, then the author's response.
The author says 'this would be closer' — note his concession.
2
Identify the objection
Find the claim that uniform motion indicates compulsion. What analogy do they use (fire, snow, food)?
3
Analyze the author's response
The author says this interpretation is 'closer' because compelled things act uniformly. Why is that not a full endorsement? Consider the context of the debate.
He does not agree that stars are compelled; he only says the argument for compulsion is stronger than the astrologers' alternative.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Why does the author include this concession? How does it serve his overall refutation?
He is showing that even if we accept the objection, it doesn't prove free choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى أنه لو قال قائل : إن ما يظهر من حركات النجوم وسيرها ودوران الفلك على نمط واحد وسجية واحدة غير مختلفة يدلُّ على أنها مجبولة على ذلك، ومضطرة إليه، ومطبوعة عليه على قول أصحاب الطباع، لكان ذلك أقرب لأن المطبوع المجبول على الفعل من شأنه أن يكون ما يُضْطَرٌ إليه على سجية واحدة وليس كذلك المتصرفُ باختياره لأنه يفعل الشيء وضده وخلافه، فتأثيرات هذه النجوم لما تؤثره على سَنَن واحد يجري مجرى تأثير النار والثلج للتسخين والتبريد على سجية واحدة وتأثير الطعام والشراب وما جرى مجرى ذلك فما ظهر من حركاتها أقرب إلى أن يدل على قول أصحاب الطباع . فأما استدلال من منهم على حياة الفلك الأعظم وهذه الأفلاك التي دونه لعظم أجرامها وضيائها وإشراقها وعلو شأنها فإنه من وساوس النفوس وذلك أن عظم الجسم وعلو مكانه وشدة إشراقه وضيائه لا يدل على كونه حياً، ظلمة الجسم ولطافته وصغر شأنه لا يدل على المنع من كونه حياً لأنه قد يكون المضيء العظيم غير حيّ والخسيس المظلم اللطيف من الأجسام حياً دراكاً كالذرّ والبق وما جرى مجرى ذلك فلا تعلق في هذا.
And upon that, if someone said: 'Indeed, what appears of the movements of the stars, their courses, and the rotation of the sphere upon one pattern and one nature, not differing, indicates that they are innate upon that, compelled to it, and imprinted upon it according to the statement of the proponents of natures,' that would be closer, because that which is imprinted and innate upon action, its state is that what it is compelled to be upon one nature, and not so is the one who acts by choice, because he does the thing, its opposite, and its contrary. So the effects of these stars, for what they effect upon one course, run in the manner of the effect of fire and snow for heating and cooling upon one nature, and the effect of food and drink and what runs in that course. So what appears of their movements is closer to indicating the statement of the proponents of natures. As for the inference of those of them who infer the life of the greatest sphere and these spheres below it due to the magnitude of their bodies, their light, their radiance, and the loftiness of their station, it is from the whisperings of souls. And that is because the magnitude of the body, the loftiness of its place, the intensity of its radiance and its light do not indicate its being alive. The darkness of the body, its subtlety, and the lowliness of its station do not indicate prevention from its being alive, because it may be that the great luminous one is not alive, and the base dark subtle of bodies is alive, perceiving, like the ant, the mosquito, and what runs in that course. So there is no relevance in this.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a two-part refutation. First, the author presents a hypothetical objection: an astrologer might argue that the regular, uniform motions of the stars and spheres indicate that they are compelled by nature (tab‘) and not free agents. The author surprisingly concedes that this interpretation is actually closer to the truth ('aqrab), because compelled things act uniformly, while a free agent can do contrary actions. The effects of stars are uniform like fire (heating) and snow (cooling), which are natural not voluntary. Thus, the objection actually supports those who say stars act by nature, not by choice. Second, the author refutes the astrological argument that the life of the heavens is proven by the greatness, luminosity, and loftiness of celestial bodies. He dismisses this as 'whisperings of souls' (wasāwis al-nufūs), because physical properties like size and light do not entail life; a huge luminous body can be lifeless (like a star? actually he means the celestial bodies themselves), while small dark bodies like ants can be alive and perceptive. Thus, no connection.

Key Terms
طبع
اضطرار
اختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the author agrees with the proponents of natures that stars are compelled.
Correction: The author only says the objection is closer to the proponents' position; he does not endorse that position. His goal is to show that the objection fails to prove free will.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that the objection that stars are compelled by nature is 'closer' (aqrab)?
A) Because it uses logical inference.
B) Because compelled things act uniformly, unlike voluntary agents.
C) Because the stars are too large to be alive.
D) Because it is the view of the philosophers.

Key Takeaway
Uniform motion alone does not prove free will; it can be explained by nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your daily routines—prayer, work, sleep—are highly uniform. Does this passage challenge you to examine whether your acts of worship are truly voluntary choices or mere habits? What would change if you acted with conscious intention tomorrow?
?
The objector uses uniformity to argue for compulsion. Are there areas in your life where you have mistaken your own uniformity (e.g., in sin or virtue) as inevitable, rather than a choice you are making? Will you reclaim your agency today?
?
The author says a voluntary agent can do the thing, its opposite, and its contrary. In what area of your life are you afraid to exercise your freedom to choose the opposite of what you usually do? What holds you back?

Size and Luminosity Do Not Prove Life
Second part of the refutation: invalid inference from size and light to life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the argument that the heavens' size and brightness prove they are alive is fallacious.

Core Idea
Physical size and light do not indicate life.

In the second part of his refutation, Imam al-Baqillani dismisses the astrological argument that the magnitude and radiance of the celestial spheres imply they are living beings. He calls this 'whisperings of souls' and provides a simple counterexample: large, bright bodies can be lifeless, while small, dark creatures like ants are alive and perceptive. Let's see why this argument fails.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage

3
Understand the refutation
The author gives a clear counterexample: large luminous bodies can be non-living, and small dark bodies can be living. Why does this work as a refutation?
He is showing that the properties do not entail life.
4
Consider the broader implication
This refutation emphasizes that life is not deducible from physical attributes alone. How does this support the author's overall argument?
It undermines any attempt to prove the heavens are alive based on visible features.

Refutation of Astrological Causation of Seasons
The author denies that seasonal changes are caused by planets, using analogy with fire and ice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author rejects the astrological inference that planetary positions cause seasonal changes, using the analogy of fire and snow.

Core Idea
Correlation does not imply causation – a key theological principle.

This lesson examines a classic refutation of astrological claims. The author shows that just because seasonal changes correlate with the sun's position, it does not mean the sun or planets cause those changes. He draws a powerful analogy with fire and snow to expose the logical flaw.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the structure: the astrologers' claim, then the author's rebuttal.
2
Understand the analogy
Focus on how the author compares the sun's proximity to heat and farness to cold with the effect of fire (heating) and snow (cooling) on bodies. Ask: does proximity to fire cause heating in the same way the astrologers claim?
The analogy is meant to show that mere correlation does not prove causal agency.
3
Connect to broader refutation
The author notes that the same argument used against those who believe in natural causation (fī‘l al-tibā‘) applies here. This shows the consistency of his critique.
This refutes both naturalists and astrologers with one logical principle.
4
Reflect on the principle
Consider what this teaches about causality in Islamic theology. The author is not denying that God creates effects at these times; he is denying that the planets themselves are agents.
This preserves divine omnipotence while acknowledging observable patterns.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تعلقهم في إثبات تأثيرات هذه الكواكب بحمي الزمان عند قرب الشمس وبرده عند بعدها عن عالمنا وكون الاعتدال في زمن الخريف والربيع عند توسطها فإن ذلك أجمع لا يدل على أن ما يحدث في عالمنا الأمور من فعلها كما لا يدل حدوث التبريد والتسخين في الأجسام عند مجاورة الثلج والنار على أن ذلك من فعلها وكل شيء نقضنا به على القائلين بفعل الطباع بهذا الاستدلال فهو بعينه ناقض لتعلق المنجمين به.
As for their clinging in affirming the effects of these planets to the heat of the time when the sun is near and its cold when it is far from our world, and the occurrence of the equinox in the season of autumn and spring when it is in the middle, then all that does not indicate that what occurs in our world of matters is from their action, just as the occurrence of cooling and heating in bodies upon proximity to snow and fire does not indicate that that is from their action. And everything by which we refuted the statement of those who speak of the action of natures with this inference, it is exactly the same refutation for the clinging of the astrologers to it.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage refutes the astrologers' argument that the planets cause seasonal changes (heat when the sun is near, cold when far, and equinoxes at midpoints). The author argues that these correlations do not prove causation. He draws an analogy: if a body becomes cold near snow or hot near fire, we do not conclude that snow or fire caused the change, because that would be attributing effect to a mere circumstance. The same refutation he used against those who believe in natural causation (fī‘l al-tibā‘) applies here. The astrologers' inference is invalid for the same reasons.

Correction: The author's refutation is about causal agency, not about denying observable patterns. He affirms that God creates heat when the sun is near, but the sun itself is not the cause.

Key Takeaway
Seasonal changes are not caused by planets; correlation does not prove causation, as shown by the fire-snow analogy.
