Disproving Celestial Causation: Essences and Positions
Baqillani disproves astrological causation via two reductio arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's two-part logical argument that refutes the claim that celestial bodies or their positions necessitate terrestrial events.

Core Idea
Homogeneity of bodies disproves celestial causation.

Baqillani now presents a critical refutation of astrological determinism. He considers two possible mechanisms—essences or positions—and shows both lead to contradictions. This passage is a masterclass in using reductio ad absurdum within kalam reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the English translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice how Baqillani sets up two conditional statements using 'إن كانت... وجب'.
2
Identify the two conditional arguments
The passage has two main parts: (1) If events are from the essences of celestial bodies, then all bodies would produce the same effects, which is false. (2) If events are from the positions of bodies in constellations, then any body in the same position would produce the same effect, which is also false.
These are both reductio arguments: assuming the astrological claim leads to an absurd consequence.
3
Understand the premises
The first argument relies on the premise of homogeneity of all bodies (tajānus al-ajsām). The second relies on the similarity of position (kawn) for any body in a given place.
Baqillani uses the example of the Sun, Moon, Jupiter, and Saturn to illustrate.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Baqillani concludes that the astrological claim is false because neither essences nor positions can be the necessitating cause. This refutes the idea that celestial bodies are active agents causing earthly events.
The argument does not deny all influence but denies necessitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يدل على ذلك أيضاً أن هذه الحوادث الأرضية لا تخلو أن تكون واجبة عن ذوات هذه الأفلاك أو عن أكوانها في هذه البروج، فإن كانت كائنة واجبة عن ذواتها وجب أن تكون سائر الأجسام موجبة لمثل ما توجبه هذه الآثار لقيام الدليل على تجانس الأجسام وتماثل جرم المشتري وزحل والشمس والقمر؛ فكان يجب أن يكون تأثير كل شيء منها كتأثير غيره سواء؛ وكذلك سائر أجسام العالم وعلى أنه لا بد أن تكون ها هنا جهة من قبلها يصح العلم بأن ذوات هذه الأجرام وأنفسها توجب حدوث هذه الآثار وفي تعذر ذلك عليهم دليل على فساد هذه الدعوى. وإن كانت هذه الحوادث إنما تحدث عن أكوان هذه الأجسام في تلك البروج فيجب أن يكون كون القمر والمشتري في برج الحمل موجباً لما يوجبه كون الشمس فيه لأن كون كل جرم، نيراً كان أو غير نير، رطباً كان أو يابساً، في المكان من جنس كون غيره فيه، ألا ترى أن كون الزئبق في برج الحمل يجب أن يكون ككون الشمس فيه على مذهبهم في إيجاب الأكوان.
And from what indicates that also is that these terrestrial events are not free from being necessitated by the essences of these spheres or by their positions in these constellations. For if they are existent, necessitated by their essences, then it would be necessary that the rest of the bodies necessitate the like of what these effects necessitate, because the evidence stands for the homogeneity of bodies and the similarity of the body of Jupiter, Saturn, the Sun, and the Moon. So it would be necessary that the effect of each thing of them be like the effect of the other equally, and likewise the rest of the bodies of the world. And upon that, there must be here a direction from which it is valid to know that the essences of these bodies and themselves necessitate the occurrence of these effects, and in the impossibility of that for them is evidence of the corruption of this claim. And if these events only occur from the positions of these bodies in those constellations, then it would be necessary that the position of the Moon and Jupiter in the constellation of Aries necessitate what the position of the Sun in it necessitates, because the position of every body, be it luminous or not luminous, moist or dry, in a place is of the same kind as the position of another in it. Do you not see that the position of Mercury in the constellation of Aries must be like the position of the Sun in it according to their doctrine concerning the necessitation of positions?
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents a two-part logical argument. The author considers two possibilities for how terrestrial events could be caused by celestial bodies: either by the bodies themselves (their essences) or by their positions (akwān) in the constellations. First, if events are necessitated by the essences of celestial bodies, then because all bodies are homogeneous (mutajānisa) and similar in substance, every body should have the same effect. Since the sun, moon, Jupiter, and Saturn are all bodies, they should all cause the same effects, but they do not. Moreover, there is no known way to know that the essences specifically necessitate these effects. This impossibility (ta‘adhdhur) proves the claim false. Second, if events come from the positions of these bodies in the constellations, then any body in the same constellation should produce the same effect, because the position (kawn) of one body in a place is the same kind as the position of another. For example, Mercury in Aries should cause the same effect as the Sun in Aries, but astrologers do not claim this. Thus, the astrological theory is inconsistent.

Key Terms
ذوات
أكوان
بروج
تجانس
تماثل
إيجاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is arguing that celestial bodies have no influence whatsoever on terrestrial events.
Correction: Baqillani is specifically refuting the astrological claim of necessitation (ījāb), not denying any possible influence. The argument targets causal necessity, not all forms of influence.

Checkpoint
What is the main premise used in the first argument (against causation by essences)?
A) Celestial bodies are made of different elements.
B) All bodies are homogeneous (tajānus al-ajsām).
C) Positions in constellations are irrelevant.
D) The sun is the sole cause of earthly events.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani uses two conditional arguments to show that neither the essences nor the positions of celestial bodies can necessitate terrestrial events, thereby refuting astrological determinism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you unconsciously attribute your mood or fortune to a horoscope or planetary alignment, forgetting that only Allah has power? How will you actively combat this subtle shirk using Baqillani's logical proof?
?
When you face a setback, do you catch yourself thinking 'it's just bad luck' rather than turning to Allah? How can this lesson transform your reaction into a moment of tawheed and reliance?
?
Baqillani's argument shows that even if celestial bodies existed, they could not necessitate events. What 'celestial bodies' in your life—people, circumstances, or objects—have you wrongly believed have a necessary impact on your happiness, and how will you break that false belief today?

Refuting Astrological Causation: The Fire and Snow Analogy
Baqillani refutes astrological causation using fire and snow analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Baqillani rejects the claim that planets causally affect earthly events, and how he uses the fire and snow analogy to demonstrate that correlation does not imply causation.

Core Idea
Correlation does not imply causation: proximity does not prove agency.

Imam Baqillani presents a powerful critique of astrological determinism. He argues that the observed association between planetary positions and seasonal changes does not prove that the planets cause those changes. To clarify his point, he draws a simple analogy: fire and snow are observed to heat and cool bodies, but we do not attribute agency to them. This lesson unpacks his argument and its implications for Islamic theology of causality.

Guided Path
1
Understand the opening remark
Notice how Baqillani begins by pointing out an inconsistency: large luminous celestial bodies are not alive, while small dark creatures like ants are alive and perceptive. This sets the stage for questioning astrological claims.
This first sentence challenges the notion that celestial bodies have agency.
2
Grasp the core analogy
Read the main argument where Baqillani compares the sun's proximity to fire and snow. Just as fire does not cause heat by its own nature (in the Ash'ari view), the sun does not cause seasons. The observed correlation is not proof of causation.
The analogy is central: fire/snow are mere occasions, not agents.
3
Connect to the broader refutation
The final sentence links this argument to previous refutations of naturalism. Baqillani asserts that the same reasoning used against those who claim natures act also refutes astrologers.
This shows the unity of his critique against all forms of necessary causation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المضيء العظيم غير حيّ والخسيس المظلم اللطيف من الأجسام حياً دراكاً كالذرّ والبق وما جرى مجرى ذلك فلا تعلق فى هذا وأما تعلقهم في إثبات تأثيرات هذه الكواكب يحمي الزمان عند قرب الشمس وبَرْدِه عند بعدها عن عالمنا وكَوْنِ الاعتدال في زمن الخريف والربيع عند توسطها فإن ذلك أجمع لا يدل على أن ما يحدث في عالمنا الأمور من فِعْلِها كما لا يدل حدوث التبريد والتسخين في الاجسام عند مجاورة الثلج والنار على أن ذلك من فعلها وكل شيء نقضنا به على القائلين بفعل الطباع بهذا الاستدلال فهو بعينه ناقض لتعلّق المنجمين به.
The great luminous (object) is not alive, and the lowly dark delicate of bodies is alive and perceptive like the ant and the gnat and what runs in that course; so there is no attachment in this. And as for their attachment in proving the effects of these planets in heating the time when the sun is near and its cold when it is far from our world and the occurrence of equinox in autumn and spring when it is in between, then all of that does not indicate that what occurs in our world of affairs is from their action, just as the occurrence of cooling and heating in bodies when adjacent to snow and fire does not indicate that that is from their action. And everything we have refuted against those who say that natures act, by this inference, is the very same refutation for the attachment of the astrologers to it.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of astrological causation. Imam Baqillani begins by noting the inconsistency in attributing life to celestial bodies: a great luminous body is not alive, while a small dark body like an ant is alive and sentient. He then addresses the astrologers' claim that planets have effects such as heating and cooling based on the sun's proximity. He argues that these phenomena do not prove that the planets are the agents of these effects — rather, they are merely associated events. The analogy is given: when we bring snow near a body, it becomes cold; when we bring fire, it becomes hot. But we do not conclude that the snow or fire causes the cold or heat; rather, they are occasions. Similarly, the occurrence of seasons with the sun's position does not mean the sun causes them. Baqillani then states that every argument used against the naturalists (who claim natures act) applies equally to the astrologers' claims.

Key Terms
الكواكب
الطباع
تأثيرات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqillani's argument denies all causal relationships and denies that fire actually burns or snow actually cools.
Correction: Baqillani does not deny the observable correlation; he denies that the objects are the true agents of change. In Ash'ari theology, Allah is the sole creator of effects, and physical objects are mere occasions.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why does the fact that cooling occurs when snow is brought near a body not prove that snow causes the cooling?
A) Because snow is not a body
B) Because correlation does not imply causation
C) Because snow is actually hot
D) Because the body is the cause

Key Takeaway
Observable correlations between celestial events and earthly seasons do not prove that the planets are the efficient causes; as with fire and snow, agency is not proven by proximity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider something in your life that you habitually attribute to a secondary cause—perhaps a lucky object, a particular habit, or even a person. Are you willing to see that as merely an occasion, while true agency belongs to Allah alone? What would change if you truly internalized that?
?
When you experience a change in your circumstances—like a season of difficulty or ease—do you instinctively look for a worldly explanation? How can Baqillani's fire and snow analogy reorient your heart toward the true Causer?
?
Baqillani states that the same refutation used against naturalists applies to astrologers. Is there an area in your life where you functionally act as a 'naturalist' or 'astrologer,' attributing power to created things? What step can you take today to strip that false attribution?

Refutation of Astrological Causation: The Homogeneity Argument
Baqillani presents a dichotomy and refutes essence-based causation by appealing to homogeneity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the homogeneity of celestial bodies undermines the claim that they cause earthly events by their essences.

Core Idea
Similar bodies cannot produce different effects if causation is by essence.

Baqillani presents a logical refutation of astrological causation. He argues that if planets cause events by their inherent essences, then all celestial bodies, being homogeneous, would produce identical effects. The observed diversity of effects shows this cannot be true. Let's examine the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the logical structure: a dichotomy followed by a conditional argument.
2
Identify the dichotomy
Baqillani divides possible causes into two: either the essences of the celestial spheres or their configurations in constellations. Find this in the text.
The phrase 'لا تخلو أن تكون' sets up the dichotomy.
3
Understand the essence case
He then takes the first possibility: if caused by essences, then homogeneous bodies (all celestial spheres) must have identical effects. Why? Because their material nature is the same.
The key principle is 'تجانس الأجسام' (homogeneity of bodies).
4
See the conclusion
Since effects are different, the premise that they are caused by essences is false. Additionally, they cannot provide a mechanism to explain how essence would produce specific effects.
Their inability to explain is itself a proof against them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يدل على ذلك أيضاً أن هذه الحوادث الأرضية لا تخلو أن تكون واجبة عن ذوات الأفلاك أو عن أكوانها في هذه البروج، فإن كانت كائنة موجبة عن ذواتها وجب أن تكون سائر الأجسام موجبة لمثل ما توجبه هذه الآثار لقيام الدليل على تجانس الأجسام وتماثل جرم المشتري وزُحَلَ والشمس والقمر ؛ فكان يجب أن يكون تأثير كل شيء منها كتأثير غيره سواء ؛ وكذلك سائر أجسام العالم وعلى أنه لا بد أن تكون ها هنا جهة من قبلها يصحُ العلم بأن ذواتِ هذه الأجرام وأنفسها توجب حدوث هذه الآثار وفي تعذر ذلك عليهم دليل على فساد هذه الدعوى.
And among what indicates that also is that these earthly events cannot but be either necessitated by the essences of the celestial spheres or by their configurations in these constellations. If they are existent necessitated by their essences, then it would be necessary that all other bodies be necessitating similar to what these effects necessitate because the proof stands for the homogeneity of bodies and the similarity of the mass of Jupiter, Saturn, the Sun, and the Moon; so it would be necessary that the effect of each of them be like the effect of the other equally; and likewise all bodies of the world. And (it is necessary) that there be a direction from which it is valid to know that the essences of these bodies and themselves necessitate the occurrence of these effects, and in their inability to do that is a proof of the corruption of this claim.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents a logical argument against the claim that heavenly bodies cause earthly events by their very essences. Baqillani sets up a dichotomy: either the effects are due to the essences of the celestial spheres (ذوات الأفلاك) or due to their positions in constellations. He first takes the case of essences. If the effects were due to their essences, then all bodies of the same nature should have the same effects. But since the celestial bodies are all of the same kind (homogeneous), their effects would be identical. However, we observe different effects from different planets, so the premise is false. Moreover, if they caused effects by essence, there would need to be a way to determine exactly how and why a particular effect follows, but they cannot provide such a mechanism. Their inability to do so is evidence against their claim.

Key Terms
ذوات الأفلاك
تجانس الأجسام
تماثل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqillani is denying all natural causation in the world.
Correction: He is specifically refuting the astrological claim that planets have inherent causal power by their essences, not denying causal relationships established by Allah's custom.

Checkpoint
What is the main premise of Baqillani's argument against effects from essences?
A) That planets are not similar
B) That similar bodies must have similar effects
C) That Jupiter is unlike Saturn
D) That the moon is not a body

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's homogeneity argument shows that if celestial bodies caused effects by essence, their effects would be identical, which is contradicted by experience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself thinking that your skills, your health, or even your prayer is effective by its own power? Where in your life have you attributed causation to created things while forgetting that Allah is the sole Creator of every effect? Will you repent from this subtle shirk today?
?
Baqillani shows that similar bodies would produce identical effects if causation were by essence. But in your life, you see different outcomes from similar situations. Is it possible that you are underestimating the direct intervention of Allah in every detail? How will you train your heart to see His hand in every difference?
?
The astrologers could not provide a mechanism for their claimed causation. What about you? Are there areas where you trust in vague explanations of 'how things work' without acknowledging that the only real mechanism is Allah's will? What would change if you lived each moment with that awareness?

The Principle of Identical Configurations
Baqillani argues that identical configurations necessitate identical effects, using analogies from everyday experience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani establishes the logical principle that two similar configurations must produce identical effects, using everyday analogies to expose a flaw in astrological causation.

Core Idea
Same position demands same effect — that’s the logical rule.

Baqillani continues his critique of astrology by assuming the astrologers' own premise: that events are caused by the configurations of planets in constellations. He then shows that this premise leads to absurd consequences. In this first part, he establishes the principle that two similar configurations must produce identical effects, using comparisons like mercury and water in a vessel, or a live coal and ice in the same place. This principle is the foundation of his reductio.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise
The astrologers claim that the configuration of a planet in a constellation causes certain events. Baqillani takes this premise and asks: if that is so, then any body in that configuration should have the same effect.
He uses 'كواجب' to indicate necessity.
2
Examine the examples
He gives three analogies: mercury and balsam in a vessel vs water; a live coal vs ice in a place; the Moon and Sun in Aries.
For each, the configuration (being in a specific place) is identical, so the effect should be identical.
3
Apply the rule to planets
He then generalizes: two similar things must have the same effect. So any planet in the same constellation should have the same effect as another.
Notice the example of Moon and Sun both in Aries to show that if they have the same configuration, they must have the same effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كانت هذه الحوادث إنما تحدث عن أكوان هذه الأجسام في تلك البروج فيجب أن يكون كون القمر والمشتري في برج الحمل موجباً لما يوجبه كون الشمس فيه لأن كون كل جرم نيّراً كان أو غير نير، رطباً كان أو يابساً، في المكان من جنس كون غيره فيه، ألا ترى أن كون الزئبق والبلسان في القدح والمكان المعيّن من جنس كون الماء فيه؟ وكذلك كونُ الجمرة في المكان من جنس كون قطعة الثلج فيه؟ وإذا ثبت ذلك وجب أن يكون كون كل كوكب في برج من هذه البروج موجباً لمثل ما أوجبه كون غيره فيه لأن الشيئين المتماثلين يجب أن يكون تأثيرهما والموجب عنهما واحداً، ألا ترى أنه لما كان كون القمر في برج الحمل من جنس كون الشمس فيه، وجب أن يصير كل واحد من الكونين في تلك المحاذاة وذلك البرج بعينه؟ فكذلك يجب أن يكون سائر موجبات الكونين واحداً، وكذلك السوادان المتماثلان يجب أن يكون تأثيرهما في المحل والمنظر تأثيراً واحداً ولا يجوز أن يكون أحدهما مسوداً والآخر مبيضاً. وكذلك الحرارتان والبرودتان لا يجوز أن تكون إحداهما مسخّنة والأخرى مبردة. فإذا كان ذلك كذلك، وجب أن يكون تأثير الشمس إذا كانت في برج الحمل هو تأثير المَرِّيخ وزُحَلَ إذا كانا فيه، وأن يكون كوننا نحن ذلك البرج، لو وجدنا فيه، أو بعضُ الحجارة موجباً من التأثير مثل الموجب عن كون الشمس فيه، وإن لم يصح وجود نجم من هذه الطوالع في مكان الآخر وفلكه وجب أن يؤثر كون الشمس في البرج والدقيقة في الدرجة إذا كانت مقارنة لزُحَلَ أو مقابلة لبعض الطوالع ما تؤثره إذا لم تكن تلك في المقابلة والمقارنة وفي إجماعهم على بطلان ذلك دليل على أن هذه التأثيراتِ لا يجوز أن تكون واجبةً عن ذوات هذه الأفلاك ولا
And if these events occur only from the configurations of these bodies in those constellations, then it would be necessary that the configuration of the Moon and Jupiter in the constellation Aries necessitate what the configuration of the Sun in it necessitates, because the configuration of every body - whether luminous or not, moist or dry - in a place is of the same kind as the configuration of another in it. Do you not see that the configuration of mercury and balsam in the vessel and the specific place is of the same kind as the configuration of water in it? And likewise the configuration of a live coal in a place is of the same kind as the configuration of a piece of ice in it? And if that is established, then it would be necessary that the configuration of every planet in a constellation of these constellations necessitate similar to what the configuration of another in it necessitates, because two similar things must have their effect and what is necessitated by them be one. Do you not see that since the configuration of the Moon in Aries is of the same kind as the configuration of the Sun in it, then it would be necessary that each of the two configurations become in that alignment and that same constellation? Thus it would be necessary that the rest of the requisites of the two configurations be one. And likewise two similar blacknesses must have their effect in the place and appearance be one effect, and it is not permissible that one of them be blackening and the other whitening. And likewise two heats and two colds are not permissible that one of them be heating and the other cooling. So if that is so, then it would be necessary that the effect of the Sun when it is in Aries be the effect of Mars and Saturn when they are in it, and that our own configuration (if we were to exist in it) or some stones would necessitate an effect like the effect necessitated by the configuration of the Sun in it. And if it is not valid for any star from these ascendants to exist in the place and sphere of another, then it would be necessary that the configuration of the Sun in the constellation and the minute in the degree, if it is in conjunction with Saturn or in opposition to some ascendants, to effect what it effects when those are not in opposition and conjunction. And in their consensus on the falsehood of that is a proof that these effects cannot be necessitated by the essences of these celestial spheres nor...
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents Baqillani's second refutation, this time assuming that effects come from the positions of planets in constellations. He uses a reductio ad absurdum: if the configuration in a constellation determines the effect, then any body in that same configuration should produce the same effect. He gives examples: mercury in a vessel and water are in the same 'place' and should have the same effect; a live coal and ice in the same place should have the same effect (absurd). Similarly, if the Moon and Sun are both in Aries, they should have the same effect. He extends the analogy to physical qualities: two similar blacknesses must have the same effect (both blacken), two heats both heat, etc. Therefore, if the Sun, Mars, and Saturn are in the same constellation, they would all have the same effect. Even if we or stones were in that constellation, they would have the same effect. This is obviously false, so the premise is false. The astrologers themselves agree that such effects are not observed, which proves that the effects are not necessitated by the essences or positions of the celestial bodies.

Key Terms
أكوان
بروج
تماثل
تأثير
كواجب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Baqillani is denying any correlation between planetary positions and events.
Correction: He is only denying that positions are efficient causes; he accepts that they may be associated without being causative.

Checkpoint
What logical principle does Baqillani establish in this passage?
A) That planets cause events by their nature
B) That two similar configurations must produce identical effects
C) That the Moon and Sun are identical in substance
D) That astrology is a valid science

Key Takeaway
Identical configurations logically require identical effects, which is the key premise in Baqillani's reductio against astrological causation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you assume that similar situations will produce the same outcomes, forgetting that Allah alone creates each event? How can you break this habit and remember that nothing is forced upon Him?
?
When you see patterns in nature, do you instinctively attribute them to inherent causes rather than to Allah's direct and constant power? What practical step can you take today to shift your mindset?
?
If you truly believed that every effect is directly from Allah, how would your reaction to unexpected events change? Will you commit to pausing before attributing anything to 'natural causes' and instead say, 'Allah willed it'?

Absurd Consequences and the Final Proof
Baqillani completes his reductio by showing absurd consequences and citing astrologers' consensus as proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the astrologers' own consensus on the falsehood of identical effects to prove that the stars are not efficient causes.

Core Idea
Astrologers agree that different planets in the same constellation don't cause the same effects — so positions aren't the cause.

In the second part of his argument, Baqillani draws the logical conclusion from the principle of identical configurations: if the Sun, Mars, and Saturn are in the same constellation Aries, they would all produce the same effect. Even we or stones, if placed in that constellation, would have the same effect. This is clearly false, and the astrologers themselves would agree. Their consensus on this falsehood provides the final proof that the effects are not necessitated by the essences of the celestial bodies or their positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the logical conclusion
Baqillani applies the principle to specific planets: Sun, Mars, Saturn in Aries.
Since their configurations are the same (all in Aries), they must have the same effect.
2
Extend to absurdity
He then considers ourselves or stones in that constellation, showing that even non-luminous objects would have the same effect as the Sun.
This absurd consequence indicates the premise is false.
3
Introduce the astrologers' consensus
Baqillani notes that the astrologers themselves agree that such identical effects do not occur.
This consensus is empirical evidence against the causal claim.
4
Draw the final inference
The falsehood of identical effects proves that the effects are not necessary outcomes of the essences or positions of the celestial spheres.
This is the conclusion of the reductio.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The astrologers' own consensus disproved their system. Is there a belief in your life that you cling to despite your own deeper principles contradicting it? What would it cost you to honestly examine it now?
?
Baqillani uses pure reason to expose falsehood without appealing to revelation. Are you willing to apply the same ruthless logic to your assumptions about God's actions in your life? Identify one assumption and test it today.

Proof That Celestial Effects Are Not Necessary
Baqillani disproves necessary causation by showing that similar configurations do not produce similar effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the principle of similar causes producing similar effects to refute astrological determinism.

Core Idea
Similar causes must have similar effects; since they don't, celestial effects are not necessary.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani presents a powerful refutation of astrological determinism. He uses the principle that if celestial effects were necessary properties of the stars or their positions, then similar configurations would always produce identical outcomes. By showing that this is not the case—different planets in the same zodiac sign produce different effects—he concludes that such effects cannot be necessary or natural.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the English translation. Let Baqillani's argument unfold naturally.
Notice the logical structure: principle, examples, application, consensus, conclusion.
2
Identify the key analogy
Baqillani uses the example of the sun and moon both being in the sign of Aries. According to the principle of similarity, they should produce identical effects if causation were necessary.
This analogy is central to the proof.
3
Understand the principle of similar causes
The principle states that two similar things must have the same effect. Baqillani extends this to blackness, heat, and cold: two blacknesses cannot be one blackening and the other whitening.
This is a logical axiom in kalam.
4
Notice the consensus argument
Baqillani notes that astrologers themselves agree that different planets in the same sign (e.g., Mars and Saturn in Aries) have different effects. This consensus is used as evidence against necessary causation.
The consensus refutes the claim of necessity.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The effects cannot be necessary (wajib), nor can they be from the essences of the spheres, nor by nature or power/choice. Therefore, attributing effects to the spheres is invalid.
The argument clears the way for occasionalism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت ذلك وجب أن يكون كون كل كوكب في برج من هذه البروج موجباً لمثل ما أوجبه كون غيره فيه لأن الشيئين المتماثلين يجب أن يكون تأثيرهما والموجب عنهما واحداً، ألا ترى أنه لما كان كون القمر في برج الحمل من جنس كون الشمس فيه، وجب أن يصير كل واحد من الكونين في تلك المحاذاة وذلك البرج بعينه؟ فكذلك يجب أن يكون سائر موجبات الكونين واحداً، وكذلك السوادان المتماثلان يجب أن يكون تأثيرهما في المحل والمنظر تأثيراً واحداً ولا يجوز أن يكون أحدهما مسوداً والآخر مبيضاً. وكذلك الحرارتان والبرودتان لا يجوز أن تكون إحداهما مسخنة والأخرى مبردة. فإذا كان ذلك كذلك، وجب أن يكون تأثير الشمس إذا كانت في برج الحمل هو تأثير المريخ وزحل إذا كانا فيه، وأن يكون كوننا نحن ذلك البرج، لو وجدنا فيه، أو بعض الحجارة موجباً من التأثير مثل الموجب عن كون الشمس فيه، وإن لم يصح وجود نجم من هذه الطوالع في مكان الآخر وفلكه وجب أن يؤثر كون الشمس في البرج والدقيقة في الدرجة إذا كانت مقارنة لزحل أو مقابلة لبعض الطوالع ما تؤثره إذا لم تكن تلك في المقابلة والمقارنة وفي إجماعهم على بطلان ذلك دليل على أن هذه التأثيرات لا يجوز أن تكون واجبة عن ذوات هذه الأفلاك ولا عن ذوات أكوانها في البروج ولا كائنة عنها على سبيل الطبع ولا على وجه القدرة والاختيار فلا معنى إذاً لنسبة هذه الآثار إلى الأفلاك.
And if that is established, then it must be that the being of every planet in a sign of these signs necessitates the like of what the being of another in it necessitates, because two similar things must have their effect and what is necessitated by them be one. Do you not see that since the being of the moon in the sign of Aries is of the same genus as the being of the sun in it, then each of the two beings in that alignment and that same sign must become alike? So likewise all the necessitata of the two beings must be one. And likewise two similar blacknesses must have their effect on the place and appearance be one effect, and it is not permissible that one be blackening and the other whitening. And likewise two heats and two colds: it is not permissible that one be heating and the other cooling. So if that is so, then it must be that the effect of the sun when it is in the sign of Aries is the effect of Mars and Saturn when they are in it, and that our being in that sign, if we were to exist in it, or some stones, would necessitate an effect like the effect necessitated by the sun's being in it. And if it is not correct for any star of these ascendants to exist in the place and sphere of another, then it must be that the sun's being in the sign and minute in the degree, when it is conjunct with Saturn or opposite some ascendants, effects what it effects when those are not in opposition and conjunction. And their consensus on the invalidity of that is evidence that these effects cannot be necessary from the essences of these spheres, nor from the essences of their beings in the signs, nor produced from them by way of nature, nor by way of power and choice. So there is no meaning, then, to attributing these effects to the spheres.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a proof by analogy and consensus. Baqillani argues against astrological determinism by showing that if celestial effects were necessary due to the nature of the celestial bodies or their positions, then similar configurations (same zodiac sign, same alignment) would produce identical effects. He uses examples: the sun and moon in Aries should produce the same effect; two instances of blackness must both blacken; heat must heat, cold must cool. Since astrologers acknowledge that different planets in the same sign produce different effects (e.g., Mars and Saturn in Aries do not act like the sun), this shows that the effects are not necessary properties of the spheres or their positions. The consensus of astrologers that such identity does not hold proves that the effects are not necessary, contingent, or natural—they are not attributable to the spheres at all.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqillani denies any celestial influence on earthly events.
Correction: He only denies necessary, natural causation, not the possibility of divinely ordained occasional influence.

Why does Baqillani argue that celestial effects are not necessary?
A) Because the sun and moon are different in essence.

Key Takeaway

What concrete step can you take today to shift that reliance?
?
Baqillani argues that if similar causes necessitated similar effects, then every identical situation would yield the same outcome. Yet you experience variety and exceptions. How does this inconsistency in the world point you to the freedom of God's will rather than to randomness? Baqillani's First Refutation of Celestial Causation
Baqillani refutes the analogy between celestial influence and the cause-effect relationship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's first argument against the analogy between celestial influence and the cause-effect relationship: that the 'ruling' (ḥukm) is nothing other than the cause itself.

Core Idea
The effect is not a separate entity; it is identical to the cause itself.

An objector argues that celestial bodies influence earthly events just as knowledge necessitates the attribute 'knowing'—not by action or nature. Baqillani responds with a sharp logical point: the so-called 'effect' (ḥukm) is not a distinct thing; it is merely the cause itself. If that were the case, then celestial effects would be nothing more than the bodies or their positions—an absurdity nobody accepts.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the objector's analogy and Baqillani's immediate rebuttal.
The objector tries to defend celestial causation by comparing it to logical causation.
2
Identify the objector's claim
The objector says celestial effects are like 'the knower as knowing'—necessitated by the cause but not by action or nature. Identify this analogy.
3
Understand Baqillani's first point
Baqillani argues that the 'ruling' (ḥukm) is not separate from the cause. For example, 'the knower as knowing' is just the existence of knowledge. So if celestial bodies are causes, their effects would be identical to themselves or their positions.
This is a key distinction: cause and effect are not always two distinct entities.
4
Grasp the absurd consequence
If celestial effects were like logical effects, then earthly events would be the same as the spheres—which is clearly false. That shows the analogy fails.
5
Reflect on the refutation
Consider why this first rebuttal is effective. It undermines the entire analogy by collapsing the cause-effect distinction.
Baqillani will offer more arguments, but this one strikes at the core.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل منهم: ما أنكرتم أن يكون تعلق هذه الآثار بالأفلاك ونسبتها إليها على حسب تعلق الحكم بالعلة ونسبته إليها وذلك ككون العالم عالماً والقادر قادراً والمتحرك متحركاً، الواجب عن العلم والقدرة والحركة لا على سبيل الفعل ولا على سبيل الطبع؟ قيل له: لا يجب ما قلته من وجوه. أحدها أن الحكم عندنا الذي زعمت أنه موجب عن العلة ليس هو شيئاً غير العلة، بل كون العالم عالماً والمتحرك متحركاً ليس بمعنى أكثر من وجود الحركة والعلم فقط، فيجب على هذا ألا تكون هذه الحوادث في الأرض معنى سوى ذوات الكواكب أو كونها في تلك البروج وهذا جهل لا يصير أحد إليه.
For if a proponent among them says: 'What prevents you from saying that the attachment of these effects to the spheres and their attribution to them is according to the attachment of the ruling (ḥukm) to the cause and its attribution to it, such as the existence of the knower as knowing, the powerful as powerful, and the mover as moving, which is necessitated by knowledge, power, and motion—not by way of action nor by way of nature?' It is said to him: 'What you have said is not necessary, from several aspects. One of them is that the ruling (ḥukm) in our view, which you claim is necessitated by the cause, is nothing other than the cause. Rather, the existence of the knower as knowing and the mover as moving is not a meaning more than the existence of motion and knowledge alone. So on this basis, these events on earth must not be a meaning other than the essences of the planets or their being in those signs—and this is ignorance that no one would accept.'
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector (an astrologer or natural philosopher) tries to defend celestial causation by analogy: just as knowledge necessitates the attribute 'knowing' (al-ʿālim) without being an act or a natural process, so the spheres might necessitate effects on earth. Baqillani gives the first of multiple rebuttals. He argues that in the cause-effect relationship (like knowledge and being knowing), the 'effect' (ḥukm) is not a separate entity; it is merely the existence of the cause itself. For example, the knower's being knowing is nothing more than the existence of knowledge. Thus, if the celestial bodies were causes, their effects would not be separate events on earth; they would be identical to the bodies themselves or their positions—which is absurd and no one claims. Therefore the analogy fails.

Correction: Baqillani shows that in logical causation, the effect (ḥukm) is not separate from the cause; e.g., 'knowing' is just the existence of knowledge.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

?

Baqillani's Second Answer and a New Objection
Baqillani gives the second answer and presents a new objection from analogy with divine actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's second argument against the celestial cause-effect analogy and identify the new objection from divine actions, noting that the reply is missing in the available text.

Core Idea
The effect of a cause cannot be separated from its own locus; this refutes the celestial analogy.

Baqillani continues his refutation of the astrologers' cause-effect analogy with a second argument, emphasizing that a cause's effect must remain attached to its own subject. He then encounters a challenging objection: God's actions (like justice) are separate from His Essence yet produce effects. The text breaks off mid-objection, leaving the resolution for a later lesson.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully

The passage contains a full argument followed by an incomplete objection.

Find the objection: 'Does not action, justice, and grace necessitate the agent being acting/just, even though they are separate from the essence?' Consider why this might be a strong counterargument.

والوجه الآخر أن الحكم الواجب عن العلة لا يصح أن ينفصل عن العلة التي توجد بها العلة فلذلك لم يجز أن تكون الحركة ولا الذات حكماً لا عن موجب لكون غير من وجدت به متحركاً وكذلك العلم والإرادة وسائر ما يوجب لا يجوز أنه يوجب حكماً في غير محله فيجب إذا كان ذلك كذلك ألا توجب أنفس هذه الأفلاك وكونها في البروج شيئاً من التأثيرات إلا في أنفسها ومواضع أكوانها، وفي العلم بانفصال هذه الأفعال عن ذوات البروج ومحل أكوانها دليل على فساد تشبيههم ما ادعوه بالعلة والحكم. فإن قالوا: أفليس الفعل والعدل والتفضل يوجب كون الفاعل فاعلاً والعادل عادلاً، وإن لم يوجد ذلك في محله؛ لأن الفعل والعدل من الله تعالى منفصل من ذاته تعالى؟
And the other aspect: that the ruling necessitated by the cause cannot be separated from the cause by which the cause exists. Therefore motion and the essence cannot be a ruling necessitated by something for the existence of one other than the one by which it is moved. And likewise knowledge, will, and everything that necessitates: it is not permissible that it necessitates a ruling in other than its place. So if that is so, then these spheres themselves and their being in the signs must not necessitate any of the effects except in themselves and the places of their beings. And in the knowledge of the separation of these acts from the essences of the signs and the place of their beings, there is evidence of the corruption of their analogy of what they claim with cause and ruling. If they say: 'Does not action, justice, and grace necessitate the existence of the agent as acting and the just as just, even though that is not found in its place? Because action and justice from Allah, exalted, are separate from His Essence?'
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage contains Baqillani's second answer to the cause-effect analogy and a new objection. In the second answer, he argues that the effect (ḥukm) of a cause cannot be separated from the cause's own locus. For example, motion makes the moving thing moving; it does not produce a separate effect in another thing. Similarly, knowledge and will necessitate their effects only in their own subject. Thus, if celestial bodies were causes, their effects would be confined to themselves (e.g., their own positions), not on earth. The fact that we observe effects on earth separate from the celestial bodies disproves the analogy. Then a new objection is raised: God's actions (like creating justice) are separate from His Essence and produce effects (e.g., being just) in the agent without residing in the agent's essence. How does that differ? The objection is cut off; Baqillani's answer is not provided in this window. This indicates a possible counterargument that Baqillani would need to address, perhaps by distinguishing divine attributes from celestial causation.

Correction: Baqillani's two answers are complementary: the first redefines what counts as an effect, the second argues that even if they were effects, they'd be confined to the cause's own location.

Denying Celestial Causation and the Analogy Objection
Baqillani states his denial and presents the opponent's analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's initial denial of celestial causation and the opponent's analogy comparing it to the necessary property of a cause.

Core Idea
Effects are not caused by celestial bodies; the opponent's analogy is flawed.

Baqillani begins by asserting that earthly events are not produced by celestial spheres, whether by nature or by divine choice. He then anticipates an objection: why not see it as a necessary concomitant like knowledge necessitates being knowledgeable? This lesson presents the claim and the objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a statement followed by an objection.
2
Identify Baqillani's initial position
Find where Baqillani denies that effects come from celestial bodies. Note the two modes he rejects: by nature (ṭab‘) and by power and choice (qudra wa ikhtiyār).
This is the foundation of his refutation.
3
Understand the opponent's analogy
The opponent compares the relation to that of a cause (ʿilla) and its necessary property (ḥukm). Study the examples (knowledge, power, motion) and how they necessitate their properties necessarily, not by act or nature.
The key is that the property is inseparable and necessary.
4
Reflect on the force of the objection
Ask yourself: why might this analogy seem plausible? The opponent is trying to show that the relation could be necessary without being an act or natural compulsion.
Baqillani will answer this in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن ذوات أكوانها في البروج ولا كائنة عنها على سبيل الطبع ولا على وجه القدرة والاختيار فلا معنى إذاً لنسبة هذه الآثار إلى الأفلاك. فإن قال قائل منهم : ما أنكرتم أن يكون تعلق هذه الآثار بالأفلاك ونسبتها إليها على حسب تعلق الحكم بالعلة ونسبته إليها وذلك ككون العالم عالماً والقادر قادراً والمتحرك متحركاً، الواجب عن العلم والقدرة والحركة لا على سبيل الفعل ولا على سبيل الطبع ؟ قيل له : لا يجب ما قلته من وجوه . أحدها أن الحكم عندنا الذي زعمت أنه موجب عن العلة ليس هو شيئاً غير العلة، بل كونُ العالم عالماً والمتحرك متحركاً ليس بمعنى أكثر من وجود الحركة والعلم فقط، فيجب على هذا ألا تكون هذه الحوادث في الأرض معنى سوى ذوات الكواكب أو كونها في تلك البروج وهذا جهل لا يصير أحد إليه. والوجه الآخر أن الحكم الواجب عن العلة لا يصح أن ينفصل عن العلة التي توجد بها العلة فلذلك لم يجز أن تكون الحركة حكما عن الذات موجة لكون غير من وجدت به متحركاً وكذلك العلم والإرادة وسائر ما يُوجِبُ لا يجوز أنه يوجب حكماً في غير محله فيجب إذا كان ذلك كذلك ألا توجب أنفس هذه الأفلاك وكونُها في البروج شيئاً من التأثيرات إلا في أنفسها ومواضع أكوانها، وفي العلم بانفصال هذه الأفعال عن ذوات البروج ومحل أكوانها دليل على فساد تشبيههم ما ادعوه بالعلة والحكم .
Regarding the essences of their configurations in the zodiacal signs, and they are not generated from them by way of nature nor by way of power and choice, so there is no meaning to attributing these effects to the celestial spheres. If a speaker among them says: 'What prevents you from holding that the connection of these effects to the celestial spheres and their attribution to them is according to the connection of the necessary property (al-hukm) to the cause (al-‘illa) and its attribution to it, like the world being knowing, the powerful being powerful, and the moving being moving, which are necessitated by knowledge, power, and motion, not by way of act nor by way of nature?' It is said to him: What you have said is not necessary for several reasons. One of them is that the necessary property (al-hukm) which you claim is necessitated by the cause is nothing other than the cause; rather, the world being knowing and the moving being moving is not a meaning more than the existence of motion and knowledge alone. Therefore, on this basis, these events on earth would be nothing other than the essences of the stars or their being in those zodiacal signs, and this is ignorance that no one would adopt. The other aspect is that the necessary property necessitated by the cause cannot separate from the cause by which the cause exists; therefore it is not permissible for motion to be a necessary property of the essence necessitating that something other than that through which motion exists be moving. Likewise, knowledge, will, and everything that necessitates cannot necessitate a necessary property in something other than its proper place. Therefore, if this is the case, then these celestial spheres themselves and their being in the zodiacal signs cannot effect any influence except in themselves and the places of their configurations. And knowledge of the separation of these actual effects from the essences of the zodiacal signs and the locus of their configurations is evidence of the corruption of their analogy of what they claim to the cause and the necessary property.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. The author first states his own position: the effects observed on earth cannot be attributed to celestial bodies (stars, planets, etc.) either by nature (tab‘) or by divine power and choice (qudra wa ikhtiyār). Therefore, attributing these effects to the celestial spheres is meaningless. Then he presents the opponent's objection: why can't the relation between celestial bodies and earthly events be like the relation between a cause (al-‘illa) and its necessary property (al-hukm)? For example, knowledge necessarily makes one knowing, power makes one powerful, and movement makes one moving. These are necessary concomitants, not acts of choice or nature. The author answers with two points. First, the necessary property (ḥukm) is not something additional to the cause; it is identical to the existence of the attribute. For example, 'being knowing' is nothing more than the existence of knowledge. Therefore, if celestial bodies were causes, their effects would be nothing more than their own existence or their being in signs, not separate earthly events. That would be absurd, so no one would accept it. Second, a necessary property cannot exist apart from the cause that produces it; it always remains within the cause. For instance, motion makes only that which moves moving; it cannot make someone else moving. Similarly, knowledge and will cannot produce an effect outside the subject that possesses them. Hence, if celestial bodies were causes, their influence would be confined to themselves, not to earthly events. The fact that we observe the effects occurring separately from the celestial bodies proves their analogy is false.

D) They are like a tool in God's hand.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani rejects celestial causation and presents the opponent's analogy that effects may follow necessarily, like properties from causes.

?

Does your speech reflect total trust in Allah as the only cause, or does it reveal hidden assumptions of secondary causation? What will you change starting today?

Baqillani's Two Refutations of the Analogy
Baqillani provides two refutations of the opponent's analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's two arguments refuting the analogy of celestial bodies to causes producing necessary effects.

Core Idea
Necessary properties are inseparable from their causes, so celestial bodies cannot affect earthly events.

Here, Baqillani answers the objection with two powerful arguments. First, the necessary property (ḥukm) is not distinct from the cause; it is identical to the existence of the attribute. Second, a necessary property cannot leave its cause and affect something else. Therefore, celestial bodies cannot produce effects on earth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage (the answer part)
Read the Arabic from 'قيل له' to the end. Note that it begins with 'It is said to him' indicating the author's response.
The answer contains two distinct arguments introduced by 'أحدها' and 'والوجه الآخر'.
2
Identify the first argument: ḥukm is identical to the cause
Baqillani argues that the necessary property is nothing other than the cause itself. For example, 'being knowing' is just the existence of knowledge. Thus, if celestial bodies were causes, their effect would be themselves, not separate events.
This shows the absurdity of transferring effects to the earth.
3
Identify the second argument: ḥukm cannot leave its cause
A necessary property must remain in the cause; it cannot affect something else. Motion only makes the moving thing moving, not another thing. Similarly, celestial bodies can only influence themselves.
This directly refutes the possibility of earthly effects.
4
Understand the conclusive evidence
Baqillani ends by stating that the observed separation of effects from the celestial bodies disproves the analogy. If they were real causes, effects would be inseparable.
This is an empirical argument in addition to the logical ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن ذوات أكوانها في البروج ولا كائنة عنها على سبيل الطبع ولا على وجه القدرة والاختيار فلا معنى إذاً لنسبة هذه الآثار إلى الأفلاك. فإن قال قائل منهم : ما أنكرتم أن يكون تعلق هذه الآثار بالأفلاك ونسبتها إليها على حسب تعلق الحكم بالعلة ونسبته إليها وذلك ككون العالم عالماً والقادر قادراً والمتحرك متحركاً، الواجب عن العلم والقدرة والحركة لا على سبيل الفعل ولا على سبيل الطبع ؟ قيل له : لا يجب ما قلته من وجوه . أحدها أن الحكم عندنا الذي زعمت أنه موجب عن العلة ليس هو شيئاً غير العلة، بل كونُ العالم عالماً والمتحرك متحركاً ليس بمعنى أكثر من وجود الحركة والعلم فقط، فيجب على هذا ألا تكون هذه الحوادث في الأرض معنى سوى ذوات الكواكب أو كونها في تلك البروج وهذا جهل لا يصير أحد إليه. والوجه الآخر أن الحكم الواجب عن العلة لا يصح أن ينفصل عن العلة التي توجد بها العلة فلذلك لم يجز أن تكون الحركة حكما عن الذات موجة لكون غير من وجدت به متحركاً وكذلك العلم والإرادة وسائر ما يُوجِبُ لا يجوز أنه يوجب حكماً في غير محله فيجب إذا كان ذلك كذلك ألا توجب أنفس هذه الأفلاك وكونُها في البروج شيئاً من التأثيرات إلا في أنفسها ومواضع أكوانها، وفي العلم بانفصال هذه الأفعال عن ذوات البروج ومحل أكوانها دليل على فساد تشبيههم ما ادعوه بالعلة والحكم .
Regarding the essences of their configurations in the zodiacal signs, and they are not generated from them by way of nature nor by way of power and choice, so there is no meaning to attributing these effects to the celestial spheres. If a speaker among them says: 'What prevents you from holding that the connection of these effects to the celestial spheres and their attribution to them is according to the connection of the necessary property (al-hukm) to the cause (al-‘illa) and its attribution to it, like the world being knowing, the powerful being powerful, and the moving being moving, which are necessitated by knowledge, power, and motion, not by way of act nor by way of nature?' It is said to him: What you have said is not necessary for several reasons. One of them is that the necessary property (al-hukm) which you claim is necessitated by the cause is nothing other than the cause; rather, the world being knowing and the moving being moving is not a meaning more than the existence of motion and knowledge alone. Therefore, on this basis, these events on earth would be nothing other than the essences of the stars or their being in those zodiacal signs, and this is ignorance that no one would adopt. The other aspect is that the necessary property necessitated by the cause cannot separate from the cause by which the cause exists; therefore it is not permissible for motion to be a necessary property of the essence necessitating that something other than that through which motion exists be moving. Likewise, knowledge, will, and everything that necessitates cannot necessitate a necessary property in something other than its proper place. Therefore, if this is the case, then these celestial spheres themselves and their being in the zodiacal signs cannot effect any influence except in themselves and the places of their configurations. And knowledge of the separation of these actual effects from the essences of the zodiacal signs and the locus of their configurations is evidence of the corruption of their analogy of what they claim to the cause and the necessary property.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. The author first states his own position: the effects observed on earth cannot be attributed to celestial bodies (stars, planets, etc.) either by nature (tab‘) or by divine power and choice (qudra wa ikhtiyār). Therefore, attributing these effects to the celestial spheres is meaningless. Then he presents the opponent's objection: why can't the relation between celestial bodies and earthly events be like the relation between a cause (al-‘illa) and its necessary property (al-hukm)? For example, knowledge necessarily makes one knowing, power makes one powerful, and movement makes one moving. These are necessary concomitants, not acts of choice or nature. The author answers with two points. First, the necessary property (ḥukm) is not something additional to the cause; it is identical to the existence of the attribute. For example, 'being knowing' is nothing more than the existence of knowledge. Therefore, if celestial bodies were causes, their effects would be nothing more than their own existence or their being in signs, not separate earthly events. That would be absurd, so no one would accept it. Second, a necessary property cannot exist apart from the cause that produces it; it always remains within the cause. For instance, motion makes only that which moves moving; it cannot make someone else moving. Similarly, knowledge and will cannot produce an effect outside the subject that possesses them. Hence, if celestial bodies were causes, their influence would be confined to themselves, not to earthly events. The fact that we observe the effects occurring separately from the celestial bodies proves their analogy is false.

Refutation of Tawallud as a Basis for Astrological Causation
Baqillani responds to an objection by denying the validity of generated acts (tawallud).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Baqillani rejects the concept of generated acts (tawallud) in both human and divine acts, and how this refutes an analogy used to support astrological causation.

Core Idea
Tawallud (generated acts) is invalid; thus astrology cannot rely on it.

This passage presents a key objection against Baqillani's denial of astrological influence. The objector suggests that celestial events might cause earthly events in the same way that a generated act (tawallud) follows from its cause. Baqillani's response is uncompromising: he denies the very validity of tawallud in any realm, thus cutting off the analogy at its root. Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Understand the analogy the objector proposes between astrological causation and the relation of a generated act to its cause.
The objector asks: 'Why not admit that events relate to celestial spheres like a generated act relates to its cause?'
2
Identify Baqillani's first reason
He states that generation (tawallud) is false and not established in acts of creatures or the Creator.
This is the first of multiple reasons (though only one is given here).
3
Consider the implications
If tawallud is invalid, the analogy collapses. This refutes any causal link between celestial spheres and earthly events via generation.
Baqillani's denial is absolute—tawallud is not valid for any being.
4
Reflect on the broader significance
This shows the Ash'ari position that all acts are directly created by Allah, not through generated causes.
It underscores that causes do not produce effects by themselves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال منهم قائل: ما أنكرتم أن يكون تعلّق هذه الحوادث بالأفلاك على حسب تعلق الفعل المتولّد بما ولده من الأسباب؟ قيل: أنكرنا ذلك لأمور: أحدها أن التولد عندنا باطل غير ثابت في أفعال الخلق ولا في أفعال الخالق تعالى فلا معنى لتشبيه الأمور به.
But if someone among them says: "What prevents you from admitting that the occurrence of these events to the celestial spheres is like the relation of an act generated (al-fi'l al-mutawallid) to its causes?" It was said: "We reject that for [several] reasons: One of them is that generation (tawallud) according to us is false and not established in the acts of creatures nor in the acts of the Creator, Exalted; so there is no meaning to comparing matters to it."
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. The objector challenges the author's denial of astrological causation by comparing it to the concept of 'generated acts' (tawallud), where an effect is produced from an immediate cause (e.g., fire burning). The objector suggests that celestial bodies cause earthly events in a similar manner. Baqillani replies by first denying the validity of tawallud itself. He states that generation (tawallud) is not established in the acts of either creatures or God. Therefore, there is no basis for the analogy. This is a foundational refutation: if the very mechanism of 'generation' is rejected, the entire argument for astrological causation collapses at its root.

Baqillani's Refutation of Astrological Causation
Baqillani analyzes two possible modes of astrological generation and refutes both.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Baqillani refutes astrological causation by examining two possible modes of generation from celestial bodies and demonstrating their impossibility.

Core Idea
Astrology's causal claims collapse under the weight of their own internal contradictions.

Imam al-Baqillani turns the tables on astrologers by examining the very mechanism they assume. He proposes two possible ways celestial bodies could cause events—through their essences or through their positions—and shows that both lead to absurd consequences. This lesson walks through his elegant refutation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possibilities
Read the opening of the passage where Baqillani states the two possible modes of generation: from the essences (dhawat) of the spheres or from their positions (akwan) in the zodiac. Note that this bifurcation covers all possibilities.
This is a standard method of refutation: exhaust the options and refute each.
2
Analyze the refutation of essence-based causation
Baqillani argues that if essences cause effects, then all bodies of the same genus (jism) would produce identical effects. This would require the sun to generate what the moon generates, and rocks to generate celestial effects, which is absurd.
The argument relies on the homogeneity of physical bodies.
3
Analyze the refutation of position-based causation
If positions cause effects, then the same position (e.g., Aries) should produce the same effect regardless of which planet occupies it. But astrologers deny that Jupiter and the moon have the same effect in Aries, contradicting their own assumptions.
Baqillani uses a reductio ad absurdum by assuming the astrologers' own framework.
4
See the final blow: precise location parity
Baqillani extends the argument: even if the sun and moon were in the exact same minute of the same constellation, their effects would have to be identical because the two celestial bodies are of the same genus. This further undermines any claim of astrological influence.
This strengthens the refutation by addressing the most specific scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الآخر أن هذه الحوادث لا تخلو أن تكون متولّدة عن ذوات الأفلاك وجواهرها أو عن أكوانها في البروج، فإن كانت متولدة عن ذواتها فقد ثبت عند كل أحد ممن ينفي التولد ومن يثبته أن ذوات الأجسام لا تولد شيئاً وعلى أنه لو جاز توليدها لهذه التأثيرات لوجب توليد الشمس لمثل ما يولده القمرُ وتوليد الصخور الصلاب وسائر الأجسام لما تولده ذواتُ هذه الأفلاك لأنها كلها من جنس واحد ، وهذا باطل عندنا وعندهم. وإن كانت هذه الحوادث متولّدة عن أكوان هذه الأفلاك في البروج وجب أن يكون كون الشمس في برج الحمل مولداً لما يولده كون المشتري والقمر فيه وذلك باطل عندهم. وإنما وجب ذلك لما قلناه من وجوب تجانس هذه الأكوان في المكان الواحد مع تغاير الكائنين فيه وفي بطلان هذا دليل على فساد ما ظنوه من ذلك، ويجب إن لم يصح كون الشمس سائرة في برج القمر وكائنةً في الدقائق التي يكون فيها القمر، أن يكون كون الشمس في تلك الدقيقة من فلكها ومن البروج مؤثراً لذلك الحادث متى وُجد، سواء كان في مقابلة الكائن فيه شيء أو لم يكن، وسواء رَبّعَ الكوكب أو سدسه لأن الكوكبين في ذلك المكان لا شك من جنس واحد فبطل بذلك ما قالوه.
And the other aspect is that these events cannot but be either generated from the essences (dhawat) of the celestial spheres (al-aflak) and their substances (jawhariha), or from their positions (akwan) in the zodiac (al-buruj). If they are generated from their essences, then it is established with everyone, including those who deny generation (tawallud) and those who affirm it, that the essences of bodies do not generate anything. And moreover, if it were permissible for them to generate these effects, then the sun would necessarily generate what the moon generates, and solid rocks and all other bodies would generate what the essences of these spheres generate, because they are all of one genus. This is false according to us and according to them. And if these events are generated from the positions of these spheres in the zodiac, then the sun's position in Aries (al-Hamal) must generate what the positions of Jupiter (al-Mushtari) and the moon generate in it, and that is false according to them. And it is necessarily so because of what we said about the necessity of homogeneity (tajanus) of these positions in one place despite the difference of the two positioned bodies in it. And in the falsity of this is evidence of the corruption of what they assumed from that. And it is necessary, if the sun's being in the constellation of the moon and being in the minutes in which the moon is is not valid, that the sun's position in that minute of its sphere and of the zodiac be effective for that event whenever it occurs, whether there is something opposite to it or not, and whether the star is in quartile (rabba'a) or sextile (saddasa), because the two stars in that place are undoubtedly of one genus. Thus what they said is refuted.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation by considering two possible ways astrological generation could occur. The author (Baqillani) first states the two possibilities: events are either generated from the essences (substances) of the celestial bodies or from their positions in the zodiac. He then refutes each. 

1. **Generation from essences**: If events came from the physical substances of the spheres, then since all bodies are of the same genus (jism), any body should produce the same effects. But the sun does not produce the same effects as the moon, and rocks do not produce celestial effects. This shows the impossibility.
2. **Generation from positions**: If events come from the positions of the spheres in the zodiac, then the same position should always produce the same effect regardless of which planet occupies it. For example, if the sun in Aries produces a certain effect, then Jupiter or the moon in Aries should produce the same effect, which is false astrologically. The argument then extends to a more specific scenario: if the sun and moon share the same precise location (same degree and minute), then their effect must be identical, which is absurd. Thus, both possibilities lead to contradictions, refuting astrological causation.

ذوات
أكوان
بروج
تجانسة
مقابلة
تربيع
تسديس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Baqillani is rejecting only one possibility but accepting the other.
Correction: He refutes both possibilities equally, showing both are impossible.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, if events are generated from the essences of celestial bodies, what would be a necessary consequence?
A) The sun would generate the same effects as the moon.
B) The planets would have no effect.
C) Only the moon would have effects.
D) The zodiac signs would lose their power.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes astrology by showing that both possible causal mechanisms lead to contradictions, proving it cannot be a valid source of knowledge.

If the stars cannot cause anything, then what hidden patterns or superstitions do you quietly rely on? Are you willing to abandon them completely, even if it feels uncomfortable?

Baqillani’s Refutation of Astrological Causation: The Contact Requirement
Baqillani proves that generated acts require contact, which planets lack, thus refuting astrological causation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that planets cannot cause effects in our world because they lack the necessary contact required for generated actions.

Core Idea
For an effect to be generated, the cause must touch the effect — planets do not, so they cannot affect us.

Baqillani uses a clever argument against those who claim that planets influence earthly events. He examines their own theory of ‘generation’ (tawallud) and shows that it requires direct or indirect contact between cause and effect. Since planets never touch us or anything that touches us, they cannot generate any effects in our world. This lesson unpacks that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it, then read the translation. Notice the logical flow: principle, application, reductio, conclusion.
Pay attention to the key terms: مماسة, التولد, اختراع.
2
Understand the principle of tawallud
Identify the key claim: an agent acting by generation must touch the object directly or indirectly. This is a principle Baqillani borrows from the proponents of tawallud.
Baqillani is not endorsing tawallud; he is using it as a hypothetical to refute astrologers on their own terms.
3
Apply the principle to planets
See how Baqillani applies this to deny planetary effects: since planets do not touch us or anything that touches us, they cannot generate effects in us.
4
Explore the reductio argument
Baqillani offers a symmetrical argument: if planets could affect us without contact, we could affect them similarly – which is absurd. This strengthens his case.
This reductio shows the inconsistency of allowing planetary influence without contact.
5
Grasp the conclusion
Understand the final rejection: there is absolutely no action or effect for the planets and spheres. The argument is conclusive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى أن الفاعل في غيره على سبيل التولد لا يفعل فيه إلا بأن يماسه أو يماس ما ماسه؛ ومحال عند أصحاب التولد أن يُخترع فيه الفعل اختراعاً بغير مماسة له ولا مماسة لما ماسه فيجب إذا كان كذلك ألا يصح فعل هذه الأفلاك فينا وتأثيراتها في أنفسنا وعالمنا إلا بأن تماسنا أو تماس ما ماسنا لأنه لو جاز أن تفعل فينا بالتولد على غير هذه السبيل لجاز وصح أن نفعل نحن أيضاً فيها تأثيرات وحوادث من غير أن نماسها أو نماس ما ماسها وفي تعذر ذلك واستحالته دليل على استحالة فعل هذه الكواكب فينا على هذه السبيل وإذا بطل ذلك أنه لا فعل ولا تأثير لهذه الكواكب والأفلاك بحال بتةً.
And moreover, the agent in another thing by way of generation (tawallud) does not act in it except by touching it or touching what touched it. And it is impossible according to the proponents of generation that an act be originated in it without touching it or touching what touched it. Therefore, if this is the case, then the action of these spheres upon us and their effects in our souls and our world cannot be valid except by their touching us or touching what touches us. Because if it were permissible for them to act upon us by generation in any other way, then it would also be permissible and valid for us to act upon them with effects and events without touching them or touching what touches them. And the impossibility and absurdity of that is evidence for the impossibility of the action of these planets (al-kawakib) upon us in this way. And when that is refuted, then there is absolutely no action or effect for these planets and spheres whatsoever.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a proof based on the nature of 'generated acts' (tawallud) as understood by its proponents. The author (Baqillani) first establishes a principle: in tawallud, the agent must have direct or indirect contact with the object. He then applies this to astrological causation. The spheres do not come into physical contact with us or anything that touches us, so they cannot generate effects in us by tawallud. He then adds a clever reductio: if the spheres could affect us without contact, then symmetrically we would be able to affect them without contact, which is obviously false. Therefore, the claim that planets have any effect on earthly events is completely invalid. The passage ends with a strong conclusion: there is absolutely no action or effect for the planets and spheres.

Key Terms
مماسة
التولد
اختراع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqillani accepts tawallud as a valid concept.
Correction: Baqillani only uses tawallud as a hypothetical borrowed from its proponents to refute astrologers on their own terms. He does not endorse it.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is required for an agent to act by way of generation (tawallud)?
A) The agent must be closer to the affected object.
B) The agent must touch the object or something that touches it.
C) The agent must be the same genus as the object.
D) The agent must be in the same zodiac sign.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of planetary influence is proven by the logical requirement of contact for any generated effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself attributing events in your life to distant causes like 'luck', 'bad vibes', or 'cosmic forces' without considering the actual mechanism? How does Baqillani's requirement of contact challenge you to take responsibility for what directly touches your life and to rely solely on Allah?
?
Baqillani uses a symmetric argument: if planets could affect us without contact, then we could affect them. Reflect: Do you believe you can affect things beyond your reach through mere will or emotion? What does that say about your assumptions of causation, and how does this lesson call you to purify your tawhid?
?
The passage concludes that there is absolutely no action or effect for planets at all. Have you ever felt powerless due to astrological predictions or celestial events? How does this truth free you from fear of creation and redirect your trust to the Creator alone?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
